font-weight: normal; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">of the Constitution.</span></span></p><p class="MsoTitle" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 31.5pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 31.5pt;"><span class="FontStyle22"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-font-kerning: 0pt; font-weight: normal; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">II. that the </span></span><span class="FontStyle34"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif; mso-font-kerning: 0pt; font-weight: normal; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">High </span></span><span class="FontStyle22"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-font-kerning: 0pt; font-weight: normal; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Court Division erred in law in failing to consider </span></span><span class="FontStyle34"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif; mso-font-kerning: 0pt; font-weight: normal; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">that </span></span><span class="FontStyle22"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-font-kerning: 0pt; font-weight: normal; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">the writ-petitioner with <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">mala fide</em> </span></span><span class="FontStyle29"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-font-kerning: 0pt; font-weight: normal; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold; font-style: normal; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">intention </span></span><span class="FontStyle22"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-font-kerning: 0pt; font-weight: normal; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">attempted to obtain relief indirectly which she </span></span><span class="FontStyle15"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-font-kerning: 0pt; font-weight: normal; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">could not get directly.</span></span></p><p class="MsoTitle" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 31.5pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 31.5pt;"><span class="FontStyle15"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-font-kerning: 0pt; font-weight: normal; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">III. that </span></span><span class="FontStyle19"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif; mso-font-kerning: 0pt; font-weight: normal;">the </span></span><span class="FontStyle15"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-font-kerning: 0pt; font-weight: normal; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">High Court Division erred in law in </span></span><span class="FontStyle30"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-font-kerning: 0pt; font-weight: normal; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold; font-style: normal; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">directing </span></span><span class="FontStyle22"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-font-kerning: 0pt; font-weight: normal; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">to revoke the impugned decision and to allow the writ-petitioner to commence her </span></span><span class="FontStyle30"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-font-kerning: 0pt; font-weight: normal; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold; font-style: normal; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">job </span></span><span class="FontStyle22"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-font-kerning: 0pt; font-weight: normal; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">by observing that Rules may be framed keeping a provision for “show cause notice” </span></span><span class="FontStyle34"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif; mso-font-kerning: 0pt; font-weight: normal; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">and she could only be removed upon service of a show cause </span></span><span class="FontStyle32"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-font-kerning: 0pt; font-weight: normal; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">under the </span></span><span class="FontStyle31"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-font-kerning: 0pt; font-weight: normal; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold; font-style: normal; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">new </span></span><span class="FontStyle19"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif; mso-font-kerning: 0pt; font-weight: normal;">Rule if </span></span><span class="FontStyle15"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-font-kerning: 0pt; font-weight: normal; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">so framed, which is contrary to an established principle of law.</span></span></p><p class="MsoTitle" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 31.5pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 31.5pt;"><span class="FontStyle15"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-font-kerning: 0pt; font-weight: normal; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">IV. that the writ petition was not maintainable in view of Article 117 of the Constitution, and the High Court Division erred in law in making the Rules absolute.” </span></span></p><p class="MsoTitle" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-outline-level: body-text; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 31.5pt list .5in; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif; mso-font-kerning: 0pt;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">6.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">                </span></span></span><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: Arial; mso-font-kerning: 0pt; font-weight: normal; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Mr. </span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: Arial; mso-font-kerning: 0pt; font-weight: normal;">Murad Reza, learned Additional Attorney General with Mr. Sheikh Saifuzzaman, learned Deputy Attorney General, </span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: Arial; mso-font-kerning: 0pt; font-weight: normal; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">appearing on behalf of the appellants, made submissions in line with the grounds upon which leave was granted. He further submitted that the respondent had submitted several applications for extension of her leave and those were finally decided against her giving reasons. Her application dated 11.03.1998 to consider her special circumstances were also considered and the Circular dated 30.05.2001 shows that the Government exercised discretion but decided against her. He further submitted that this is a case where the service of the writ-petitioner ceased by operation of rule 34 of BSR and hence there is no violation of article 135 of the Constitution which relates to removal from service. Hence, question of giving notice prior to removal as contemplated in article 135 is not relevant or applicable in the facts of the instant case. The learned Additional Attorney General lastly submitted that the writ-petitioner acted <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">mala fide</em> in making her applications for extension while still abroad. By reference to the decisions in 41 DLR (AD) 30 and 44 DLR (AD) 319, he submitted that in the facts and circumstances of the case, equity was not in favour of the writ-petitioner.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 31.5pt list .5in; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span class="FontStyle11"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Book Antiqua';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">7.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">                </span></span></span></strong></span><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Mr. <span style="mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Pankaz Kumar Kundu</span>,<span style="mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"> learned Advocate, appearing on behalf of the respondents made submissions in support of the impugned judgement and order of the High Court Division. He submitted </span></span><span class="FontStyle11"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">that the present petitioners consumed the stipulated time of the present </span></span><span class="FontStyle12"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">respondent No.1 rendering her out of time to </span></span><span class="FontStyle11"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">agitate her grievance before the Administrative Tribunal as per the provision of section 4 of the Administrative Tribunal Act, </span></span><span class="FontStyle12"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">1980 </span></span><span class="FontStyle11"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">and as such respondent No.1 had no equally efficacious remedy other than invoking jurisdiction under article 102 of the Constitution. He further submitted that rule 34 of the BSR is violative of the fundamental rights of respondent No.1 guaranteed under articles 27, 29, 31 and 40 of the Constitution and the impugned termination of the present respondent No.1 from the post of Dental Surgeon is nothing but a glaring instance of <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">mala fide </em>and arbitrary application of the said rule. He further submitted that petitioner No.1 issued the impugned notice and subsequent circular regarding termination of respondent No.1 from service without issuing any show cause notice upon her or giving her any opportunity </span></span><span class="FontStyle12"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">of </span></span><span class="FontStyle11"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">being heard in person in violation of the fundamental principles of natural justice as well as in violation of the provision of article 135(2) of the Constitution. He further submitted that the impugned notice and subsequent circular issued by petitioner No.1 regarding termination of respondent No.1 from service is <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">ex-facie</em> illegal inasmuch that the appointing authority of respondent No.1 is the President of the People's Republic of Bangladesh. He further submitted that the impugned order, inactions of the present petitioners and their subsequent actions are violative of the principles of legitimate expectation. He further submitted that respondent No.1 is doubly victimised due to the impugned order of termination inasmuch as she is neither in a position to serve in any government institution nor can she practice in the related field using the PhD </span></span><span class="FontStyle14"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Degree </span></span><span class="FontStyle12"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(obtained<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>from Japan) unless </span></span><span class="FontStyle11"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">or </span></span><span class="FontStyle12"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">until </span></span><span class="FontStyle11"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">she is provided an equivalence certificate from BMDC in accordance with BPSC decision 1993, whereas the </span></span><span class="FontStyle12"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">requirement </span></span><span class="FontStyle11"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">for obtaining an equivalence certificate is 2­ years’ experience on the relevant subject in any government institution of Bangladesh. He further submitted that the petitioners did not allow respondent No.1 to join her service most illegally and arbitrarily, although her service was not terminated with the approval of the </span></span><span class="FontStyle13"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">President </span></span><span class="FontStyle11"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">of </span></span><span class="FontStyle13"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Bangladesh (appointing authority </span></span><span class="FontStyle11"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">of the respondent) and due to the <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">mala fide</em> action of the petitioners, respondent No.1 is now at the verge of retirement without pay and other benefits, which is not </span></span><span class="FontStyle13"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">only violative </span></span><span class="FontStyle11"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">of the </span></span><span class="FontStyle13"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">fundamental </span></span><span class="FontStyle11"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">rights, it is also violative of one of the fundamental principles of State policy enshrined under Article 20(1) </span></span><span class="FontStyle13"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">of </span></span><span class="FontStyle11"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">the Constitution. He further submitted that petitioner No.1 issued the impugned circular on 16.04.2006 with a <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">malafide</em> intention curing the defect of earlier circular dated 30.05.2001 with regard to termination of the writ petitioner-respondent from service, which was issued long five years ago, without assigning any reason as to what steps they took during that 5 year period. He further submitted that the impugned order of termination (Annexure - I) was issued most arbitrarily, illegally and with a <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">mala fide</em> intention just to frustrate the purpose of the earlier writ petition and to cause prejudice to the writ petitioner-respondent. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 31.5pt list .5in; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">8.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">                </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">We have considered the submissions of the learned Additional Attorney General for the appellants and the learned Advocate appearing for respondent No.1, perused the impugned judgement of the High Court Division and other connected papers on record.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 31.5pt list .5in; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">9.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">                </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">From the impugned judgements, it appears that the High Court Division observed that the power conferred by rule 34 was so unjust and unreasonable that it could be asserted without hesitation that Parliament could not be taken to have authorised it. Failure to insert the requirement of show cause notice made the Rule all the more fatal. The High Court Division also observed that rule 34 is repugnant to what article 135 of the Constitution provides. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 31.5pt list .5in; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">10.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Article 135(2) provides that a </span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-fareast-language: EN-GB;">person who holds any civil post in the service of the Republic shall not be dismissed or removed or reduced in rank until he has been given a reasonable opportunity of showing cause why that action should not be taken. We are inclined to agree with the learned Additional Attorney General that the writ-petitioner’s case is not one of dismissal, removal or reduction in rank. Hence, the provisions of article </span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">135 of the Constitution are not relevant or applicable. Hence, the finding that rule 34 of the BSR is repugnant to article 135(2) and that writ-respondents concerned should have followed the mandatory provision of that article while drafting rule 34 by inserting therein a requirement to allow the service holder a right to be heard, is misconceived, where the service holder’s service was declared to have ceased on her remaining outside the country for more than 5 years.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 31.5pt list .5in; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">11.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">The High Court Division made the <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">Rules Nisi</em> absolute having found rule 34 of BSR not only <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">ultra vires</em> article 135 of the Constitution, but also unreasonable and directed rule 34 to be to set aside, and also directed the writ-respondents to revoke the impugned order and allow the writ-petitioner to commence her job. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 31.5pt list .5in; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">12.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">However, since we have observed that the writ-petitioner’s case is not one of removal or dismissal, we are of the view that the decision of the High Court Division to declare rule 34 of BSR as <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">ultra vires</em> article 135 of the Constitution, is not correct. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 31.5pt list .5in; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">13.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">The learned Additional Attorney General submitted that if any Government servant spends more than five years at a stretch away from his job, then his employment comes to an end, even if the absence is with leave. He submitted that in the instant case the respondent had leave for a total period of one year. After that she requested extension of her leave, but no extension was granted. Thus she spent more than five years in Japan without leave. Hence her service automatically came to an end. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 31.5pt list .5in; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">14.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Rule 34 of the BSR provides as follows:</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: 31.5pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 27.0pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: SutonnyBanglaMJ;">ÔÔ34 NUbvi we‡kl Ae¯’v we‡ePbv c~e©K miKvi Ab¨iƒc †Kvb wm×vš— bv wb‡j, evsjv‡`‡k d‡ib mvwf©‡m Kg©iZ _vKvi †¶Î e¨ZxZ, Ab¨Î, QywUmn A_ev QywU e¨wZZ GKvwaµ‡g cvuP ermi Kg© nB‡Z Abycw¯’Z _vKvi ci GKRb miKvix Kg©Pvixi PvKwii Aemvb nB‡e|Ó </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 31.5pt list .5in; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">15.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">From the wording of the rule it is clear that when absence from work exceeds five years, be the absence with or without leave, the service of a Government servant will come to an end. However, the Government may make a different decision upon taking into consideration any special circumstances. Hence, this automatic ceasing of the service is subject to the ability of the Government to take a different decision in the light of special circumstances. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 31.5pt list .5in; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">16.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">We find from the records that the writ-petitioner’s leave of absence for further study was extended to 30.06.1997. She then applied for a further extension till 31.03.2001 in order to complete her PhD. That would take her total period of absence from Bangladesh to 5 years 3 months and 7 days. After returning from Japan, she submitted her joining letter on 08.04.2001. In the meantime she sent an application for extension dated 17.06.1997. Getting no response, she again wrote on 06.08.1997. On 10.02.1998 she received a reply that her earlier extension stated categorically that her leave would not be further extended and that there was no opportunity to extend her leave any further. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 31.5pt list .5in; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">17.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">The writ-petitioner then wrote to the concerned authority on 11.03.1998 to give special consideration to her application for extension. She sent several other applications for extension of her leave. However, we do not find from the response of the authority that they considered any special reason for refusing the extension for which the writ-petitioner had applied. In her letter dated 11.03.1998 the writ-petitioner mentioned special circumstances, including the study and use modern techniques of dental anaesthesia in Bangladesh. In the Proggyapon dated 30.05.2001, which was impugned in Writ Petition No.3440 of 2006, it was stated that according to rule 34 of BSR her employment ceased since she was absent from her job for more than 5 years. Although there was mention in rule 34 of BSR of the possibility of ‘the Government deciding otherwise in special circumstances’, there was nothing in the Notice to suggest that any special circumstances were considered and rejected. Hence, we are of the considered view that the authority concerned did not consider the special circumstances and thus the decision not to accept the writ-petitioner’s joining letter was without lawful authority. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 31.5pt list .5in; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">18.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">The High Court Division in Writ Petition No.5287 of 2007 set aside Circular No. </span><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: MoinaNormal;">ü¡fLj/nªPMm¡-1/1-18/2006/293</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"> dated 16.04.2006. In view of our discussion above, we are of the opinion that reference to the President was not called for in the facts and circumstances of the case. According to proviso (iii) of article 135(2) reference to the President is required where it is felt by the concerned authority that notice giving opportunity to show cause is not necessary in the interest of security of the State.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>Hence the Circular was redundant and rightly set aside by the High Court Division.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 31.5pt list .5in; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">19.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">The High Court Division also observed that the writ petitioner was absent without leave for a period of excess of the 5(five) years, but directed the respondents to revoke the decision to treat her service as having ceased and to allow her to commence her job. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 31.5pt list .5in; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">20.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">In view of the facts and circumstances discussed above, we are of the opinion that the decision of the concerned authority to treat the service of the writ-petitioner as ceased, without considering any special circumstances put forward by her, is in violation of rule 34 of the BSR. Hence, the writ-petitioner-respondent No.1 must be allowed to join her post. The writ-respondents are directed to accept the joining letter of the writ-petitioner. However, in view of her absence from service, we are of the opinion that the writ-petitioner will not be entitled to receive any arrear salary.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 31.5pt list .5in; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">21.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Accordingly, the appeals are disposed of in the light of the observations and directions detailed above. There will be no order as to costs.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 31.5pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Times-Roman;"><span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">           </span>Ed. </span></strong></p><div style="mso-element: footnote-list;"><!-- [if !supportFootnotes]--><br clear="all"/><hr align="left" size="1" width="33%"/><!--[endif]--><div id="ftn1" style="mso-element: footnote;"><p class="MsoNormal"><a href="file:///H:/article/Issue__March__19(1)/Issue__March_19__C.%20A.%20217-218%20of%2015__Muhammad%20Imman%20Ali,%20J___AD___1.doc#_ftnref1" name="_ftn1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; color: black;">CIVIL<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>APPEAL Nos. 217-218 OF<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>2015</span></u></strong></a><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; color: black;">.</span></u></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 9.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt; color: black; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">(From the separate judgements and orders dated 14th day of November, 2011 passed by the High Court Division in Writ Petition Nos.3440 of 2006 and 5287 of 2007)</span></p></div></div></div></div>
740	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">Government of Bangladesh Vs. Shireen Pervin Huq, (Md. Abdul Wahhab Miah, J.) </h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p><b>Case No:</b> CIVIL PETITION FOR LEAVE TO APPEAL No. 1594 OF 2015  </p><p><b>Judge:</b>  Md. Abdul Wahhab Miah, J, Nazmun Ara Sultana, J Muhammad Imman Ali, J Hasan Foez Siddique, J.  </p><p><b>Court:</b> Appellate Division ,</p><p><b>Advocate:</b> Mr. Mahbubey Alam, Senior Advocate instructed by Mr. Haridas Paul, Advocate-on-Record.,</p><p><b>Citation:</b>  2019(1) LNJ</p><p><b>Case Year:</b>  2015</p><p><b>Appellant:</b>  Government of Bangladesh </p><p><b>Respondent:</b>  Shireen Pervin Huq and others </p><p><b>Subject:</b>  Constitution of Bangladesh</p><p><b>Delivery Date:</b>  2019-11-27</p><!DOCTYPE html><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">APPELLATE DIVISION</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: center;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(CIVIL)</span></strong></p><table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="MsoNormalTable" style="margin-left: 5.4pt; border-collapse: collapse; mso-yfti-tbllook: 480; mso-padding-alt: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;"><tbody><tr style="mso-yfti-irow: 0; mso-yfti-firstrow: yes; mso-yfti-lastrow: yes; height: 112.85pt;"><td style="width: 104.9pt; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt; height: 112.85pt;" valign="top" width="140"><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 3.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Md. Abdul Wahhab Miah, J,</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 3.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Nazmun Ara Sultana, J</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 3.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Muhammad Imman Ali, J</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 3.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Hasan Foez Siddique, J. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 3.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;"> </span></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">11.03.2015</span></strong></p></td><td style="width: 16.1pt; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt; height: 112.85pt;" width="21"><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: center; line-height: 200%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: center; line-height: 200%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: center; line-height: 200%;"><a href="file:///H:/article/Issue__March__19(1)/Issue__March_19__C.P.%201594%20of%2015__Md.%20Abdul%20Wahhab%20Miah,%20J___AD___4.doc#_ftn1" name="_ftnref1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><span class="MsoFootnoteReference"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; font-family: Symbol; mso-ascii-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-hansi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;"><span style="mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;">}</span></span></span></a></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: center;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p></td><td style="width: 93.55pt; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt; height: 112.85pt;" width="125"><p class="MsoNormal" style="mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Government of Bangladesh</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: right; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">. . . Petitioner</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: center; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">-Versus-</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; color: black; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Shireen Pervin Huq and others</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">. . .Respondents</span></strong></p></td></tr></tbody></table><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; color: white; mso-color-alt: windowtext;">Constitution of Bangladesh, 1972</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Articles 47(3), 102(3) and 104</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 120%; tab-stops: right 210.85pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 120%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">In view of the clear bar under article 47(3) of the Constitution read with article 102(3) thereof, the High Court Division had no jurisdiction to entertain the writ petition in question and the same not being entertainable, it ought to have summarily rejected the writ petition on the ground of its maintainability. It is true that the High Court Division has not said anything as to the vires of the sections of the Act, 1973 challenged in the writ petition, but it disposed of the same in the manner as quoted hereinbefore after making some observations as stated earlier; there may be a misgiving in the mind of litigant people that a writ petition challenging a provision of the Act, 1973 or any action of the International Crimes Tribunal, is amendable to the writ jurisdiction of the High Court Division under article 102 of the Constitution. Moreso, the learned Judges cannot arrogate to themselves as advisors and it was not an act of discreet on their part to advise the writ-petitioners to redress their grievance by invoking article 104 of the Constitution.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">                        </span>. . . (7)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 115%; tab-stops: right 210.85pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 115%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Abdul Quader Mollah Vs. the Chief Prosecutor, International Crimes Tribunal Dhaka, 66 DLR (AD) 289 ref.</span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.5in; line-height: 115%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 1.0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 115%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">For the Petitioner:</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 115%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> Mr. Mahbubey Alam, Senior Advocate instructed by Mr. Haridas Paul, Advocate-on-Record.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.5in; line-height: 115%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 1.0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 115%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">For the Respondents:</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 115%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> Mr. Aktar Imam, Senior Advocate instructed by Mrs. Madhu Malati Chowdhury Barua, Advocate-on-Record</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: center; line-height: 115%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 115%;">JUDGMENT</span></u></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt;"><strong><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; font-variant: small-caps;">Md. Abdul Wahhab Miah, J:</span></u></strong> <span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">This petition for leave to appeal has been filed by writ-respondent No.1 against the order dated the 29th day of April, 2015 passed by a Division Bench of the High Court Division in Writ Petition No.3930 of 2015 disposing the same.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 115%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 115%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 115%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">From the facts disclosed in the petition, it appears that respondent Nos.1-12 herein as the petitioners (hereinafter referred to as the writ-petitioners) filed the writ petition challenging section 11(4) read with section 21 of the International Crimes (Tribunals) Act, 1973 (in short, the Act, 1973) to the extent that “these sections do not provide a right of appeal to accused contemnors” as unconstitutional and void being violative of the fundamental rights of the writ-petitioners as guaranteed in articles 26, 27, 31 and 39 of the Constitution.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 115%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: list 0in left 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 115%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">3.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 115%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">From the impugned order, it appears that the learned Attorney General made candid submission before the High Court Division that in view of the provisions of article 47(3) of the Constitution, the writ-petitioners could not challenge the vires of sections 11(4) and 21 of the Act, 1973 invoking article 102 of the Constitution in view of sub-article (3) thereof. It appears that the High Court Division noticed the provisions of articles 47(3) and 102(3) of the Constitution and itself observed <em>“Since having regard to Article 47(3) of the Constitution the petitioners are not entitled to challenge section 11(4) read with section 21 of the Act, 1973 to the extent that it does not provide right of appeal and that this Court while exercising jurisdiction under Article 102 of the Constitution cannot pass any order in view of Article 102(3) of the Constitution” </em>and then made further observation that in order to redress their grievance, the writ-petitioners were at liberty to invoke 104 of the Constitution before the Appellate Division “seeking complete justice.” In the context, the High Court Division referred the case of Abdul Quader Mollah-Vs- the Chief Prosecutor, International Crimes Tribunal, Dhaka, 66 DLR (AD) 289 and after quoting the relevant portion from the said judgment where this Division spoke about its inherent jurisdictional power and its power of doing complete justice under article 104 of the Constitution, disposed of the application under article 102 of the Constitution in the following terms:</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 115%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 115%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">“Considering the above position of facts and law as well as the observations and findings this application is accordingly disposed of.”</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 115%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: list 0in left 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 115%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">4.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 115%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Mr. Mahbubey Alam, learned Attorney General, appearing for the petitioner submits that since the High Court Division had no jurisdiction to entertain an application under article 102 of the Constitution challenging any provision of the Act, 1973, it should have rejected the application summarily as being not maintainable, instead it disposed of the same with some observations and thereby impliedly made the writ petition maintainable.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 115%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: list 0in left 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 115%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">5.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 115%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Mr. Aktar Imam, learned Counsel, appearing for the writ-petitioner-respondents, on the other hand, has submitted that the High Court Division did not say anything as to the vires of the sections of the Act, 1973 challenged before it. It simply after noting his submissions and those of the learned Attorney General and the findings and observations made in the case of Abdul Quader Mollah (supra), disposed of the writ petition. Therefore, the writ-respondent-Government had no reason to be aggrieved; the petition should be dismissed for want of cause of action.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 115%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: list 0in left 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 115%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">6.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 115%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">We have considered the submissions of the learned Attorney General and the learned Counsel for the writ-petitioner-respondents.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 115%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: list 0in left 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 115%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">7.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 115%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">In view of the clear bar under article 47(3) of the Constitution read with article 102(3) thereof, the High Court Division had no jurisdiction to entertain the writ petition in question and the same not being entertainable, it ought to have summarily rejected the writ petition on the ground of its maintainability. It is true that the High Court Division has not said anything as to the vires of the sections of the Act, 1973 challenged in the writ petition, but it disposed of the same in the manner as quoted hereinbefore after making some observations as stated earlier; there may be a misgiving in the mind of litigant people that a writ petition challenging a provision of the Act, 1973 or any action of the International Crimes Tribunal, is amendable to the writ jurisdiction of the High Court Division under article 102 of the Constitution. Moreso, the learned Judges cannot arrogate to themselves as advisors and it was not an act of discreet on their part to advise the writ-petitioners to redress their grievance by invoking article 104 of the Constitution.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 115%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: list 0in left 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 115%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">8.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 115%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">In view of the above, the last two words in the order of the High Court Division to the effect “disposed of” cannot be maintained and those two words need to be modified.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 115%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: list 0in left 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 115%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">9.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 115%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Accordingly, the order of the High Court Division stands modified to the effect that in place of “disposed of”, it shall be read as “summarily rejected”</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 115%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: list 0in left 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 115%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">10.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 115%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">This petition is disposed of accordingly.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 115%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 115%; font-family: 'Times-Roman',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: Times-Roman;">Ed. <span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span></span></strong></p><div style="mso-element: footnote-list;"><!-- [if !supportFootnotes]--><br clear="all"/><hr align="left" size="1" width="33%"/><!--[endif]--><div id="ftn1" style="mso-element: footnote;"><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><a href="file:///H:/article/Issue__March__19(1)/Issue__March_19__C.P.%201594%20of%2015__Md.%20Abdul%20Wahhab%20Miah,%20J___AD___4.doc#_ftnref1" name="_ftn1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><strong><u><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">CIVIL PETITION FOR LEAVE TO APPEAL No. 1594 OF 2015</span></u></strong></a><u></u></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 9.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(From the judgment and order dated the 29th day of April, 2015 passed by the High Court Division in Writ Petition No.3930 of 2015)</span></p></div></div></div></div>
741	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">Hajee Mohd. Khokon Miah Vs.  Md. Aklibur Rahman (Advocate), (Kashefa Hussain, J.)</h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p><b>Case No:</b> Civil Revision No. 4202 of 2016  </p><p><b>Judge:</b>  S. M. Emdadul Hoque, J And Kashefa Hussain, J</p><p><b>Court:</b> High Court Division,</p><p><b>Advocate:</b> Mr. Mohammad Anwar Hossain with  Mr. Nanda Dulal Das, Advocates.,</p><p><b>Citation:</b>  2019(1) LNJ</p><p><b>Case Year:</b>  2017</p><p><b>Appellant:</b>  Hajee Mohammad Khokon Miah</p><p><b>Respondent:</b>  Md. Aklibur Rahman (Advocate) and others  </p><p><b>Subject:</b>  Code of Civil Procedure </p><p><b>Delivery Date:</b>  2019-11-27</p><!DOCTYPE html><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">HIGH COURT DIVISION</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center; line-height: 150%;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">(CIVIL REVISIONAL JURISDICTION)</span></strong></p><table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="MsoNormalTable" style="margin-left: 5.4pt; border-collapse: collapse; mso-yfti-tbllook: 480; mso-padding-alt: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;"><tbody><tr style="mso-yfti-irow: 0; mso-yfti-firstrow: yes; mso-yfti-lastrow: yes;"><td style="width: 106.0pt; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top" width="141"><p class="MsoHeading8" style="margin: 0in -1.4pt 6.0pt 0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.3pt; font-style: normal; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">S. Emdadul Hoque, J</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: center;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">And</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; margin: 0in -7.4pt 6.0pt -5.4pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.5pt;">Kashefa Hussain, J</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"> </span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-right: -1.45pt; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" width="21"><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 150%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%; line-height: 200%; mso-ansi-language: EN-US; mso-fareast-language: EN-US;">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-ansi-language: EN-US; mso-fareast-language: EN-US;">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><a href="file:///H:/article/Issue__March__19(1)/Issue%20__March__19__C.%20R.%204202%20of%2016_Kashefa%20Hussain,%20J__4.doc#_ftn1" name="_ftnref1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><span class="MsoFootnoteReference"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: Symbol; mso-ascii-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-hansi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN-US; mso-fareast-language: EN-US; mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;"><span style="mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;">}</span></span></span></a></p></td><td style="width: 94.05pt; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" width="125"><p class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Hajee Mohammad Khokon Miah</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: right;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">. . Petitioner</span></em></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">-Versus-</span></strong></p><p class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: Mangal; mso-ansi-language: EN-US; mso-fareast-language: EN-US;">Md. Aklibur Rahman (Advocate) and others </span></p><p align="right" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: right;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: Mangal; mso-ansi-language: EN-US; mso-fareast-language: EN-US;">. . . Opposite parties</span></em></strong></p></td></tr></tbody></table><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.25pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; color: white; mso-color-alt: windowtext;">Code of Civil Procedure (V of 1908)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Order 6, Rule 17</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">By allowing the application of amendment of plaint under Order 6 Rule 17 of the Code of Civil Procedure, the suit actually also has been extended into a suit for specific performance of contract and for the execution of which an execution case is maintainable under the law. It is clear from condition No.1 and 2 of the Solenama and which forms</span></strong> <strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">part of the sole Decree that the parties agreed that in the event of failure by the defendant-opposite parties to execute the saf-kabala within 15 days in favour of the plaintiff-petitioner, the plaintiff-petitioner shall be entitled to enforce their right through an order of the court upon filing execution case. But it appears that somehow the court below upon misapplication of mind or whatsoever overlooked these materials factors especially the fact that the suit was eventually also extended and supplemented into a suit for Specific Performance of Contract and the court below wrongly ignored Condition No. 1 and 2 of the solenama upon which the court passed the sole decree and consequently issued an erroneous order<span style="letter-spacing: -1.0pt;">. . . . ( 6 )<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span></span></span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">Mr. Mohammad Anwar Hossain with </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">Mr. Nanda Dulal Das, Advocates.</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .5in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">... For the Petitioner</span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">None Appears</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .5in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">... For the Respondent</span></em></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: center; tab-stops: 333.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">JUDGMENT</span></u></strong></p><p class="MsoListParagraph" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">Kashefa Hussain, J</span></u></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">. </span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">Rule was issued at the instance of the petitioner in this Civil Revisional Application calling upon the opposite parties to show cause as to why the impugned Order No. 10 dated 27.11.2016 passed by learned Joint District Judge, 1<sup>st</sup> Court, Comilla in Title Execution Case No. 05 of 2016 should not be set aside and/or pass such other or further order or orders as to this court may seem fit and proper. </span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">The facts relevant for disposal of the Rule in short is that the plaintiff-petitioner originally filed Title Suit No. 275 of 2006 in the court of the Sadar Senior Assistant Judge, Comilla against the opposite party No. 01 praying for declaration of Title and confirmation of possession with respect to the suit land mentioned in the schedule of the plaint praying for relief to that effect. During pendency of the suit the parties reached a compromise and in pursuance of the compromise a solenama was filed along with an application for amendment of plaint under order 6 Rule 17 of the Code of Civil Procedure and the Solenama decree was passed on 03.05.2016. The application of amendment of plaint was made for addition to the suit that the title suit No. 275 of 2006 be also turned into a suit for specific performance of contract by incorporation of para 8 (kha)in the relief portion of the plaint along with a payment of Aadvolarem Court fee Condition No. 1 of the Solenama provided that within 15 days from the date of passing the decree in accordance with the Solenema the defendant shall be bound to execute and register the saf-kabala deed in favour of the plaintiff and condition No. 2 of the Solenama provided that in the event of failure of the defendant to do so the plaintiff-petitioner shall obtain the same, that is the saf-kabala deed through an execution case from the court. </span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">3.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">It is also alleged that the defendant-opposite parties did not fulfill the condition in the Solenema within the specific time of 15 days and therefore the plaintiff-petitioner in pursuance of Condition No. 2 of the Solenama filed Execution Case No. 05 of 2016 before the concerned court for approval of the draft kabala deed. But the court below rejected the application for approval of the kabala of the decreetal land by an order dated 27.11.2016.</span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">4.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">Being aggrieved by the impugned Order dated 27.04.2016 passed by the Learned Joint District Judge, 1<sup>st</sup> Court, Comilla in Title Execution Case No. 05 of 2016 rejecting the petition dated 27.11.2016 filed by the plaintiff-petitioner for approval of kabala of the decreetal land, the plaintiff-petitioner filed the instant Civil Revision which is before us for disposal. </span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">5.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">Learned Advocate Mr. Mohammad Anwar Hossain along with Mr. Nanda Dulal Das appears on behalf of the plaintiff-petitioner while none appears for the opposite parties.</span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">6.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">Learned Advocate Mr. Mohammad Anwar Hossain submits that the court below committed serious error of law and fact given that it over looked the amendment order of the suit and erroneously disallowed the petition for execution filed by the plaintiff-petitioner. He elaborates his submissions upon assertion that upon allowing the application for amendment of plaint under Order 6 Rule 17 of the Code of Civil Procedure, the suit was also turned and supplemented into a suit for Specific Performance of Contract and not merely for declaration of Title and confirmation of possession. He drew our attention to the fact that by allowing amendment of plaint the suit being supplemented into a suit for Specific Performance of Contract also, consequently, the prayer and relief sought for does not remain confined to a mere declaration of Title and confirmation of possession only. He further asserts that Title suit No. 275 of 2006 being also supplemented into a suit for Specific Performance of Contract eventually, therefore an Execution Case is maintainable and should have been allowed. He further argues that condition No. 2 of the Solenama provides that in the event of failure by the defendant-opposite party to execute the saf-kabala deed within 15 days the plaintiff-petitioner shall be entitled to file an execution case to obtain approval for saf-kabala of the decreetal land through the court, but the court below upon serious error also failed to consider this vital condition in the solenama. He concludes his submissions upon assertion that the Rule bears merit and the erroneous order of the court below be set aside and the Rule be made absolute. </span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">7.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">We have heard the learned Advocate for the plaintiff-petitioner, perused the materials on record including the Solenama, the amendment petition etc. and the impugned Order. Upon perusal of all these documents, it appears that by allowing the application of amendment of plaint under Order 6 Rule 17 of the Code of Civil Procedure, the suit actually also has been extended into a suit for specific performance of contract and for the execution of which an execution case is maintainable under the law. It is clear from condition No. 1 and 2 of the Solenama and which forms part of the sole Decree that the parties agreed that in the event of failure by the defendant-opposite parties to execute the saf-kabala within 15 days in favour of the plaintiff-petitioner, the plaintiff-petitioner shall be entitled to enforce their right through an order of the court upon filing execution case. But it appears that somehow the court below upon misapplication of mind or whatsoever overlooked these materials factors especially the fact that the suit was eventually also extended and supplemented into a suit for Specific Performance of Contract and the court below wrongly ignored Condition No. 1 and 2 of the solenama upon which the court passed the sole decree and consequently issued an erroneous Order. </span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">8.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">Considering the above facts and circumstances of the case and taking the submissions of the learned Advocate for the plaintiff-petitioner and upon perusal of all documents before us we find merit in the Rule.</span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">9.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">In the result the Rule is made absolute and the order dated 27.11.2016 passed by the learned 1<sup>st</sup> Court, Joint District Judge, Comilla in Title Execution No. 05 of 2016 rejecting the application is hereby set-aside and the executing court below is hereby directed to pass necessary orders for approval of the saf-kabala and for registration of the same accordingly.</span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">10.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">Order of stay granted at the time of issuance of the Rule is hereby vacated.</span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">11.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">Communicate the order at once.</span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">Ed. <span style="mso-spacerun: yes;"> </span></span></strong></p><div style="mso-element: footnote-list;"><!-- [if !supportFootnotes]--><br clear="all"/><hr align="left" size="1" width="33%"/><!--[endif]--><div id="ftn1" style="mso-element: footnote;"><p class="MsoNormal"><a href="file:///H:/article/Issue__March__19(1)/Issue%20__March__19__C.%20R.%204202%20of%2016_Kashefa%20Hussain,%20J__4.doc#_ftnref1" name="_ftn1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt;">Civil Revision No. </span></strong></a><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt;">4202 of 2016</span></strong></p></div></div></div></div>
742	<h2 class="blog_entry-title"> Haji Muhd. Khorshed Alam Vs.  The State, (Syed Md. Ziaul Karim, J.) </h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p><b>Case No:</b>  Criminal Revision No. 1237of 2003  </p><p><b>Judge:</b>  Syed Md. Ziaul Karim, J And Sheikh Md. Zakir Hossain, J.  </p><p><b>Court:</b> High Court Division,</p><p><b>Advocate:</b> Mrs. Sakila Rowshan,D.A.G. with Mrs. Sharmina Haque, A.A.G. and Mr. Md. Shorowardhi, A.A.G.,</p><p><b>Citation:</b>  2019(1) LNJ</p><p><b>Case Year:</b>  2014</p><p><b>Appellant:</b>  Haji Muhammad Khorshed Alam </p><p><b>Respondent:</b>  The State </p><p><b>Subject:</b>  Evidence Act </p><p><b>Delivery Date:</b>  2019-11-27</p><!DOCTYPE html><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">HIGH COURT DIVISION</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center; line-height: 150%;"><strong><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">(CRIMINAL REVISIONAL JURISDICTION)</span></strong></p><table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="MsoNormalTable" style="margin-left: 5.4pt; border-collapse: collapse; mso-yfti-tbllook: 480; mso-padding-alt: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;"><tbody><tr style="mso-yfti-irow: 0; mso-yfti-firstrow: yes; mso-yfti-lastrow: yes;"><td style="width: 106.0pt; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top" width="141"><p class="MsoHeading8" style="margin: 0in -1.4pt 6.0pt 0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.3pt; font-style: normal; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Syed Md. Ziaul Karim, J</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: center;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;">And</strong></p><p class="MsoNormal"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;">Sheikh Md. Zakir Hossain, J. </strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"> </strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-right: -1.45pt;
