padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" width="21"><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 150%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%; mso-ansi-language: EN-US; mso-fareast-language: EN-US;">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-ansi-language: EN-US; mso-fareast-language: EN-US;">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-ansi-language: EN-US; mso-fareast-language: EN-US;">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 150%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><a href="file:///H:/article/Issue__March__19(1)/Issue%20__March__19__Crl.%20Rev.%201237%20of%2003_Syed%20md.%20Ziaul%20Karim_8.doc#_ftn1" name="_ftnref1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><span class="MsoFootnoteReference"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%; font-family: Symbol; mso-ascii-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-hansi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN-US; mso-fareast-language: EN-US; mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;"><span style="mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;">}</span></span></span></a></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-ansi-language: EN-US; mso-fareast-language: EN-US;">}</span></p></td><td style="width: 94.05pt; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" width="125"><p class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Haji Muhammad Khorshed Alam</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: right;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 10.0pt;">. . . Accused-Petitioners</span></em></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">-Versus-</span></strong></p><p class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: Mangal; mso-ansi-language: EN-US; mso-fareast-language: EN-US;">The State</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: right;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: Mangal; mso-ansi-language: EN-US; mso-fareast-language: EN-US;">. . . Opposite party</span></em></strong></p></td></tr></tbody></table><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.25pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; color: white; mso-color-alt: windowtext; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Evidence Act (I of 1872)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Section 3</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">We should bear in mind, credibility of testimony oral and circumstantial, depends considerably on a judicial evaluation of the totality, not isolated scrutiny. When dealing with the serious question of guilt or innocence of persons charged with crime, the following principles should be taken into consideration.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 48.95pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">a) The onus of proving everything essential to the establishment of the charge against the accused lies on the prosecutor.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 69.1pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">b) The evidence must be such as to exclude to a moral certainty every reasonable doubt of the gilt of the accused.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 48.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">c) In matters of doubt it is safer to acquit than to condemn, for it is better that several guilty persons person should escape than that one innocent person suffer.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 52.1pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">d) There must be clear and unequivocal proof of the corpus deficit.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 71.3pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">e) The hypothesis of delinquency should be consistent with all the facts proved.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: right 210.25pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Inspite of the presumption of truth attached to oral evidence under oath if the Court is not satisfied, the evidence inspite of oath is of no avail.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">                </span>. . . (9)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 71.3pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Code of Criminal Procedure (V of 1898)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 71.3pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Sections 173, 202 and 222</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: right 210.25pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-variant: small-caps; letter-spacing: -1.0pt; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">A<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>“ </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Charge" corresponds to an "indictment" in English Law and is very much more than a mere form. It is a precise formulation of specific accusation made against a person. </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">Charge is defined as a 'precise formulation of</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> the specific accusation made against a person who is entitled to know its nature at </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">the very earliest stage. The necessity of a system</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> of written accusation specifying a definite criminal offence is the essence of criminal procedure. Charge has to be framed on the basis of the material placed before the Trial Court and while doing so the Court is not bound by the inquiry report submitted under section 202 of the Code of </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">Criminal Procedure or in a Police challan case</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> by the report submitted under section 173 of the Code of Criminal Procedure.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">   </span>. . .(10 and 11)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 71.3pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Code of Criminal Procedure (V of 1898)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 71.3pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Section 222</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: right 210.25pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">“The object of charge”- The object of framing a change is to enable the defence to concentrate its attention on the case that he has to meet, and if charge is framed in such a vague manner that the necessary ingredients of the offence with which the accused is convicted are not brought out in the charge, then the charge is defective. The framing of a proper charge is vital to a criminal trial and this is a matter on which the Magistrate or Judge should bestow the most careful attention. A charge should be carefully drawn up in accordance with the offence disclosed. The charge should be precise in its scope and particular in its details. . . . (11)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Words and Phrases</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Ground</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: right 210.25pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The word 'Ground' means basis, foundation or valid reason.  . . . (<span style="mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">12)</span></span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: 71.3pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Code of Criminal procedure (V of 1898)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: 71.3pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Section 222</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: right 210.25pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">“Conditions for framing of a charge”- conditions for framing of a charge are (i) presumption of the commission of an offence on the materials before the Court and (ii) offences triable exclusively by a competent Court.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">       </span>. . .(<span style="mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">12)</span></span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Narcotics Control Act 9XX of 1990)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Section 19(1)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: right 210.25pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">On going to the materials on record it transpires that the informant categorically narrated the manner of crime committed by the accused. The learned Judge after considering the entire materials on record rightly framed charge under Clause 2(kha) of the Table of section 19(1) of the Narcotics Control Act, 1990 against the petitioner. All that is required at the stage of framing charge is to see whether the prima-facie case regarding commission of certain offence is made out. The truth veracity and effect of evidence which prosecution proposes to adduce at the time is not to be meticulously judged at the stage of framing charge. In the instant case the accused stand indicted for offence punishable under Clause 2(kha) of the Table of section 19(1) of the Narcotics Control Act, 1990.Cognizance has been taken under the said Act. We have meticulously examined the allegations made by the informant and we find that the offence punishable under Clause 2(kha) of the Table of section 19(1) of the Narcotics Control Act, 1990 have been clearly disclosed in the instant case against the petitioner. We have gone through the grounds taken in the petition of Revision and we find that such grounds are absolutely the disputed question of facts and the same should be decided at trial. The plea of the petitioner are nothing but the defence plea. Be that as it may the proposition of law is now well settled that on the basis of defence plea or materials the criminal proceedings should not be stifled before trial; when there is a prima-facie case for going for trial.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">    </span>. . .14)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">No one appears,</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .5in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">. . . For the accused-petitioner</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Mrs. Sakila Rowshan,D.A.G. with</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Mrs. Sharmina Haque, A.A.G. and</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Mr. Md. Shorowardhi, A.A.G.</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .5in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">. . . For the State-opposite party</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: center; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">JUDGMENT</span></u></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Syed Md. Ziaul Karim, J: </span></u></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">By this Rule, accused-petitioner has challenged the legality and propriety of the order dated 07-06--2003 passed by learned Metropolitan Additional Sessions Judge, Third Court, Dhaka, (briefly as Judge) framing charge under Clause 2(Kha) of the Table of Section 19(1) of the Narcotics Control Act, 1990(briefly as Act, 1990), in Metro. Session Case no. 302 of 2002. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l2 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Facts, in brief are that the petitioner is the accused of Metro. Session Case no. 302 of 2002 under the Act, 1990. The Police after investigation submitted charge-sheet accusing him under the Act, 1990.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l2 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">3.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Eventually, the accused-petitioner was <span style="letter-spacing: -.3pt;">put on trial in the Court of Metropolitan Additional</span> Sessions Judge, Third Court, Dhaka, wherein the accused filed an application under section 265C of the Code of Criminal Procedure (briefly as the Code) for discharging him from the case. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l2 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">4.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">After hearing the learned Judge framed charge under the Act, 1990 by rejecting the said application for discharge, fixing 31-08-2003 for evidence.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l2 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">5.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Feeling aggrieved the appellant preferred the instant Revision and obtained the present Rule.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l2 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">6.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">No one appears on behalf of the petitioner to support the Rule. In view of the facts, this is an old Revision of 2003 we are inclined to take it up for disposal on merit considering the materials on record. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l2 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">7.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The learned Deputy Attorney General appearing for the State-opposite party opposes the Rule and submits that after considering the materials on record the learned Judge of the Court below rightly framed charge which calls for no interference by this Court. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l2 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">8.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">In order to appreciate her submissions we have gone through the record and given our anxious consideration to her submissions.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l2 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; color: black; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">9.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; color: black; text-transform: uppercase;">W</span></em><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; color: black;">e should bear in mind, credibility of testimony oral and circumstantial, depends considerably on a judicial evaluation of the totality, not isolated scrutiny. When dealing with the serious question of guilt or innocence of persons charged with crime, the following principles should be taken into consideration. </span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo3; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; color: black;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">a)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></em></strong><!--[endif]--><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; color: black;">The onus of proving everything essential to the establishment of the charge against the accused lies on the prosecutor.</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo3; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; color: black;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">b)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></em></strong><!--[endif]--><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; color: black;">The evidence must be such asto exclude to a moral certainty every reasonable doubt of the guilt of the accused.</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo3; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; color: black;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">c)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></em></strong><!--[endif]--><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; color: black;">In matters of doubt it is safer to acquit than to condemn, for it is better that several guilty persons should escape than that one innocent person suffer.</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo3; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; color: black;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">d)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></em></strong><!--[endif]--><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; color: black;">There must be clear and unequivocal proof of the corpus delicit.</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo3; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; color: black;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">e)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></em></strong><!--[endif]--><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; color: black;">The hypothesis of delinquency should be consistent with all the facts proved.</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; color: black;">Inspite of the presumption of truth attached to oral evidence under oath if the Court is not satisfied, the evidence inspite of oath is of no avail.</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l2 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; color: black;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">10.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; color: black;">A "Charge" corresponds to an "indictment" in English Law and is very much more than a mere form. It is a precise formulation of specific accusation made against a person. Charge has to be framed on the basis of the material placed before the Trial Court and while doing so the Court is not bound by the inquiry report submitted under section 202 of the Code of Criminal Procedure or in a Police challan case by the report submitted under section 173 of the Code of Criminal Procedure.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l2 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; color: black;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">11.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; color: black;">A charge is an important step in a criminal proceeding. It separates the inquiry stage from trial. The whole object of framing a charge is to enable the defence to concentrate its attention on the case that he has to meet, and if charge is framed in such a vague manner that the necessary ingredients of the offence with which the accused is convicted are not brought out in the charge, then the charge is defective. The framing of a proper charge is vital to a criminal trial and this is a matter on which the Magistrate or Judge should bestow the most careful attention. A charge should be carefully drawn up in accordance with the offence disclosed. The charge should be precise in its scope and particular in its details. A charge is defined as a ‘precise formulation of the specific accusation made against a person who is entitled to know its nature at the very earliest stage. The necessity of a system of written accusation specifying a definite criminal offence is the essence of criminal procedure. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l2 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; color: black;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">12.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; color: black;">The charge-sheet to which the accused is called upon to plead is a very important document. It should be drawn up and considered with extreme care and caution, so that accused may have no doubt whatever as to the offences to which he is called upon to answer and the Judge of the Appellate Court also may have no doubt upon the matter. The word ‘Ground’ means basis, foundation or valid reason. The whole object of framing a charge is to enable the defence to concentrate its attention on the case that he has to meet. Conditions for framing of a charge are (i) presumption of the commission of an offence on the materials before the Court and (ii) offences triable exclusively by a competent Court.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l2 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">13.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">In the case of Mohd. Aqil and another Vs. The State 1988 Crl. L.J. 1484 held:</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-tab-count: 2;">            </span>" Framing of charge- Matters to be considered by Court indicated.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 120%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 27.0pt;"><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 120%;"><span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">   </span>For the purpose of framing a charge the Court is required to consider judicially asto whether on consideration of the materials on record, it can be said that the accused has reasonably connected himself with the offence alleged to have been committed and that on the basis of the said material there is reasonable probability or chance of the accused<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>being found guilty of the offence alleged. If the answer is in the affirmative, the Court will be at liberty to presume "that the accused has committed the offence” as mentioned in S. 228 for the purpose of framing the charge. In finding out a prima-facie case not only the F.I.R. or complaint but even the statements of the witnesses recorded under S. 161 although the same may have been recorded after some delay during the investigation of the case are to be taken into consideration and if from all other material, a prima facie case is made out against the accused then the Magistrate has no option but to frame a charge against the accused. The Court is not expected to make a roving enquiry in the pros and cons of the matter and weigh the evidence as if he was conducting a trial. However, in a case, if two views are possible and the Judge is satisfied that evidence produced before him while giving rise to some suspicion does not give rise to grave suspicion against the accused, he will be fully within his right to discharge the accused."</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 120%; mso-list: l2 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 120%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">14.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 120%;">On going to the materials on record it transpires that the informant categorically narrated the manner of crime committed by the accused. The learned Judge after considering the entire materials on record rightly framed charge under Clause 2(kha) of the Table of section 19(1) of the Narcotics Control Act, 1990 against the petitioner. All that is required at the stage of framing charge is to see whether the prima-facie case regarding commission of certain offence is made out. The truth veracity and effect of evidence which prosecution proposes to adduce at the time is not to be meticulously judged at the stage of framing charge. In the instant case the accused stand indicted for offence punishable under Clause 2(kha) of the Table of section 19(1) of the Narcotics Control Act, 1990.Cognizance has been taken under the said Act. We have meticulously examined the allegations made by the informant and we find that the offence punishable under Clause 2(kha) of the Table of section 19(1) of the Narcotics Control Act, 1990 have been clearly disclosed in the instant case against the petitioner. We have gone through the grounds taken in the petition of Revision and we find that such grounds are absolutely the disputed question of facts and the same should be decided at trial. The plea of the petitioner are nothing but the defence plea. Be that as it may the proposition of law is now well settled that on the basis of defence plea or materials the criminal proceedings should not be stifled before trial; when there is a prima-facie case for going for trial. In view of such facts the grounds taken in the petition of Revision are not the correct exposition of law. Moreso interruption of the course of Justice will set up a wrong precedent by which the course of justice instead of being advanced readily been stifled inasmuchas the grounds advanced before us are not correct or legal exposition of law. Therefore we hold that there are sufficient grounds for proceeding against the petitioner for going for trial under Clause 2(kha) of the Table of section 19(1) of the Narcotics Control Act, 1990. To that end in view we are at one with the learned Judge of the Court below regarding framing of charge against the petitioner. In view of the above we failed to discover any merit in this Revision. Thus the Rule having no merit fails.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 120%; mso-list: l2 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 120%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">15.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 120%;">In view of foregoing narrative the Rule is discharged. The order of stay granted earlier stands vacated.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 120%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 120%;"><span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">         </span>Office is directed to communicate the order at once. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 120%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 120%;">Ed.</span></strong></p><div style="mso-element: footnote-list;"><!-- [if !supportFootnotes]--><br clear="all"/><hr align="left" size="1" width="33%"/><!--[endif]--><div id="ftn1" style="mso-element: footnote;"><p class="MsoNormal"><a href="file:///H:/article/Issue__March__19(1)/Issue%20__March__19__Crl.%20Rev.%201237%20of%2003_Syed%20md.%20Ziaul%20Karim_8.doc#_ftnref1" name="_ftn1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt;">Criminal </span></strong></a><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt;">Revision No. 1237of 2003</span></strong></p></div></div></div></div>

Respondent-Opposite party</span></em></strong></p></td></tr></tbody></table><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 12.0pt; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; color: white; mso-color-alt: windowtext;">Code of Civil Procedure (V of 190</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">8)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Order 1, Rule 10 (2)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">A civil court may add any party, if it appears to the court to be just as being a necessary party in order to enabling the court effectively and completely to be adjudicated and settled upon the question involved in the suit.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">      </span>. . . (11)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Mr. Md. Helaluddin Mollah, with</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Mrs. Syeda Farah Helal, Advocates<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span></span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .5in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">. . . For the Petitioner</span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Mr. Aminuddin, with </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Mr. Amit Das Gupta, Advocate</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .5in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">. . . For the Opposite Party Nos.1 &amp; 2</span></em></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: center; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">JUDGMENT</span></u></strong></p><p class="MsoListParagraph" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Md. Moinul Islam Chowdhury, J.</span></u></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> At the instance of the applicant-petitioner, Md. Abul Kashem, a Leave has been granted and also a Rule has been issued calling upon the opposite parties to show cause as to why the impugned judgment and order dated 30.01.2017 passed by<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>the learned Additional District Judge, 5<sup>th</sup> court, Dhaka in Civil Revision No.189 of 2016 rejection the revisional application for addition of party and thereby affirming the judgment and order dated 04.08.2016 passed by the learned Senior Assistant Judge, 6<sup>th</sup> court, Dhaka in the Title Suit No.64of 2016 should not be set aside.</span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The relevant facts for disposal of this Rule, <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">inter-alia,</em> are that the present plaintiff-opposite parties as the plaintiffs filed the Title Suit No.64 of 2016 in the court of the learned Senior Assistant Judge, 6<sup>th</sup> court, Dhaka for a decree of mandatory injunction to allot the shops situated in the multi storied market building in the Gulistan Kaptan Bazar Area as the members of the Hossain Shohid Shohrawardi Hawkers Market Malik Samity after registering with the Registrar of Trade Union on 08.07.1978<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>being No.1394/1978. The said suit was filed against the Mayer, Dhaka South City Corporation and others. The said suit is pending for disposal by the learned trial court. During pendency of the said suit, the present-applicant-petitioner filed an application under Order1 Rule 10(2) of the Code of Civil Procedure for addition of party as the defendant.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span></span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">3.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The application for addition of party contains that due to removal of market from Fulbaria to Kamalapur and due to construction of a multistoried market building, Dhaka City Corporation published an advertisement in the Daily News Paper known as Ittefaque on 07.08.1965 for allotment of shops, accordingly, Hossain Shohid Shohrawardi Dokan Malik Samity (the Samity) presented a list of members for allotment in the year of 1989-1990 and deposited Taka 1,00,000/-. However, the corporation failed to allot any shop to the members of the Samity for a long period of time. Against the delay in allotting the shops by the corporation, different members of the said Samity filed different Writ Petitions being Writ Petition No.6654 of 2009, Writ Petition No.5287 of 2009, Writ Petition No.7984 of 2009, and Writ Petition No.7904 of 2007 and those were heard together and disposed of on 26.11.2014 by this Court by giving common a direction to the Dhaka City Corporation for allotting the shop as per provision of law. Even after the aid direction from this Court, the corporation as the party in the Writ Petitions filed three Civil Petitions for Leave to Appeal in the Hon’ble Appellate Division of the Supreme Court of Bangladesh, which were dismissed by the Appex Court, therefore, the High Court Division direction remained operative. Despite the above direction, the corporation failed to allot any shop in favour of the members of the present-applicant-petitioner but the present-opposite parties as the plaintiffs filed the suit seeking a mandatory injunction for allotment of shop, therefore, as per direction of this Court in the Writ Petition, the present-applicant-petitioner is a necessary and relevant party to be added in the said suit as a defendant in order to assist the court.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span></span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">4.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">After hearing the parties the learned trial court rejected the application by passing the judgment and order dated 04.08.2016. Being aggrieved the present-petitioner filed the Civil Revision No.189 of 2016 which was heard by the learned Additional District Judge, 5<sup>th</sup> court, Dhaka who by the impugned judgment and order disallowed the application filed under Section 115(2) of the Code of Civil Procedure by affirming the judgment of the trial court. This revisional application has been filed under Section 115(4) of the Code of Civil Procedure and this Rule has been issued thereupon.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span></span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">5.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Mr. Md. Helal Uddin Mollah, the learned Advocate appearing along with Mr. Salim Ahmed for the petitioner submits that both the courts below misread the application for addition of party and misconstrued the submissions made by the present-applicant-petitioner in the court below thereby came to a wrongful conclusion to reject the application concurrently, as such, the Rule should be made absolute.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span></span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">6.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The learned Advocate also submits that there are sufficient grounds on record for the applicant-petitioner to be added as the defendant because the petitioner is a necessary party in the suit but the learned court below did not consider that the applicant-petitioner was a party in this Court and also in the Appex Court but erroneously decided the applicant-petitioner was not a necessary party, as such, the impugned order is to be set aside, as such, the Rule should be made absolute. </span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">7.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The Rule has been opposed by the present-opposite parties contending, <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">inter-alia,</em> that as per the direction passed by the High Court Division the Samity of the plaintiff filed the members list before the Ministry of Labour for its approval and the Registrar of Trade Union found that the members list filed by the plaintiff’s Samity was true. However, after that the City Corporation was not taking any action for allotting the suit shops, as such, the cause of action arose on 13.04.1985 later on 26.11.2012 and lastly on 23.11.2015, hence the suit for mandatory injunction claiming all remedies against the City Corporation. </span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">8.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Mr. A. M. Aminuddin, the learned Advocate, appearing along with the learned Advocate Mr. Amit Das Gupta for the opposite party, submits that the learned trial court properly considered the application for addition of party and the submissions of the learned Advocates and came to a lawful decision to reject the application and the learned revisional court below also considered that the present applicant-petitioner was not a necessary and relevant party to be added as his addition would cause complications in the disposal of the suit, therefore, the courts below committed no error of law and, therefore, no interference from this Court is called for. </span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">9.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The learned Advocate further submits that the plaintiff-opposite parties are the ordinary and general members of the Samity, who sought relief from the civil court as per<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>direction<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>in the writ petition filed by other members of the Samity, wherein the present-applicant-petitioner contested the suit as the respondent, therefore, the present-applicant-petitioner does not have any interest in remedy sought by the plaintiffs because the suit will be effectively and completely adjudicated by the learned trial court by settling the disputes between the present-opposite parties and the Dhaka City Corporation but this Rule has been obtained by misleading the court and the Rule should be discharged.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span></span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">10.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Considering the above submissions made by the learned Advocates appearing for the respective parties and also considering the revisional application filed under Section 115(4) of the Code of Civil Procedure along with Annexures therein, in particular, the impugned judgment and order passed by the learned revisional court below,<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>it appears to me that the present-opposite parties as the plaintiffs filed the<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>title suit with a prayer for decree of mandatory injunction to allot suit shops in Gulistan Kaptan Bazar Area<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>under the name and style of Hossain Shohid Shohrawardi Hawkers Market Malik Samity<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>by the present defendant-opposite party No.3, Dhaka South City Corporation, Dhaka. During pendency of the said suit, the present-applicant-petitioner filed an application for addition of party under Order 1, Rule 10(2) of the Code of Civil Procedure as being the President of the said Samity. The applicant-petitioner contended that having been obtained a direction from this Court in the Writ Petitions they became a necessary party in the suit filed by the present-plaintiff-opposite parties, however, the present opposite parties contended that the applicant-petitioner was not a necessary party because the cause of action of the suit arose on 13.04.1983, thereafter, on 26.11.2012 and lastly on 23.11.2015, when the corporation failed to allot shop as per the recommendation of the Ministry of Labour and preparation of a allottees lists by the Registrar of the Trade Union.</span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">11.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">In view of the above conflicting factual aspects, I consider that the present-plaintiff-opposite parties file the suit for the particular relief against the defendant who are the Dhaka City Corporation and the secretary, Ministry of Local Government of Rural Development. I am satisfied that the learned trial court can settle the disputes between the plaintiffs and defendants of the Title Suit No.64 of 2016 on the basis of the plaint and the written statement already submitted in the court wherein the present-applicant-petitioner has no cause of action or necessity for settling the dispute between the plaintiffs and defendants in the said suit. Under Order 1, Rule 10(2) of the Code of Civil Procedure a civil court may add any party, if it appears to the court to be just as being a necessary party in order to enabling the court effectively and completely to be adjudicated and settled upon the question involved in the suit.</span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">12.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The present-applicant-petitioner claimed himself as the President of the Samity and the President and obtained a direction from this Court in the Writ Petitions in its favour. However, the present-plaintiff-opposite parties have every right to claim any remedy as the individual members of the Samity if the President could not settle the matter of allotment for a long period of time with the Corporation, therefore, the present-applicant-petitioner as the President of the Samity is not a necessary party in the matter as it is not a process of the Samity but the individual members of the market pursuing their own cause. Moreover, the present-applicant-petitioner as the President has already got a direction in favour of the process of the Samity but the present-applicant-petitioner could not perform his responsibility to give any relief sought in the suit by way of settling the matter with the corporation. I, therefore, consider that any addition of the present-applicant-petitioner would certainly delay the disposal of the suit pending in the trial court which would not be justifiable to be effectively and completely adjudicated and settled the matters of the suit, therefore, the present-applicant-petitioner is not necessary and relevant party.</span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">13.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Now I am inclined to examine the findings of the learned courts. The learned trial court considered and rejected the application on the basis of the following finding:- </span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 27.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">“</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: AdarshaLipiNormal;">­j¡L¡Ÿj¡l k¡ha£u fË¢aL¡l ¢p¢Y Ll­f¡­ln­el ¢hl²­Ÿ ab¡¢f haÑj¡e clM¡Ù¹L¡l£ ®Le fri¨J² q­a Q¡e a¡ ÖfÖV euz AH ®j¡L¡Ÿj¡u HC clM¡Ù¹L¡l£l fri¨J² qJu¡l BCeNa p¤­k¡N e¡C j­jÑ j­e L¢lz</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">”</span></strong></p><p class="MsoListParagraph" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">         </span>The learned appellate court concurrently found against the present-applicant-petitioner on the basis of the following lawful finding:-</span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 27.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">“</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: AdarshaLipiNormal;">­k­qa¥ h¡c£fr fË¢afràu p¢j¢al f­r ¢hh¡c£l ¢hl²­Ÿ ®cJu¡e£ 64/16 ew j¡jm¡¢V c¡­ul L­l­R Hhw clM¡Ù¹L¡l£ E­õ¢Ma p¢j¢al HLSe ®~hd pcpÉ ®p­qa¥ h¡c£ fË¢afràu ®L¡e<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>fË¢aL¡l ®f­m a¡l p¤¢hd¡ ¢l¢ineL¡l£ fË¡ç q­hz a¡R¡s¡ j§m j¡jm¡¢V ¢e­cÑn¡aÁL ¢X¢H²l fË¡bÑe¡u j¡jm¡ qJu¡u clM¡Ù¹L¡l£l fri¨¢J²l ®L¡e L¡lZ e¡Cz jq¡j¡eÉ p¤fË£j ®L¡­VÑl ¢e­cÑ­nl B­m¡­L j§m j¡jm¡¢V Ll¡ q­u­Rz L¡­SC j§m j¡jm¡l clM¡Ù¹L¡l£l fr A¿¹Ñi¨¢J²l ®L¡e BhnÉLa¡ e¡Cz hlw clM¡Ù¹L¡l£ j§m j¡jm¡u fri¨J² q­m e¡e¡ S¢Vma¡l pª¢ÖV q­a f¡­lz</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">”</span></strong></p><p class="MsoListParagraph" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">14.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">In view of the above discussions and also after perusal of the impugned judgment and order concurrently passed by the courts below, in particular, the revisional court below I do not consider that the courts below committed any error of law. I am, therefore, not inclined to interfere into the impugned judgment and order passed by the learned appellate court. </span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">         </span>Accordingly, I do not find merit in the Leave granting order and the Rule.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span></span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">         </span>In the result, the Leave granting order is rejected and the Rule is discharged. </span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">15.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The ad-interim order of stay granted at the time of issuance of the Rule upon all further proceedings of the Title Suit No.64 of 2016 pending in the court of learned Senior Assistant Judge, 6<sup>th</sup> court, Dhaka is hereby recalled and vacated. </span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">         </span>The office is directed to communicate this judgment and order to the concerned court immediately.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Ed.</span></strong></p><div style="mso-element: footnote-list;"><!-- [if !supportFootnotes]--><br clear="all"/><hr align="left" size="1" width="33%"/><!--[endif]--><div id="ftn1" style="mso-element: footnote;"><p class="MsoNormal"><a href="file:///H:/article/Issue__March__19(1)/Issue%20__March__19__C.%20R.%20465%20of%2017_Md.%20Moinul%20Islam%20Choudhury,%20J__6.doc#_ftnref1" name="_ftn1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt;">Civil Revision No. </span></strong></a><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt;">465 of 2017</span></strong></p></div></div></div></div>
744	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">Md. Jahedul Islam Bhuiyan Vs.  Md. Abdul Rahim, (Md. Rezaul Hasan, J.) </h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p><b>Case No:</b> Civil Revision No. 7 of 2017 </p><p><b>Judge:</b>  Md. Rezaul Hasan, J</p><p><b>Court:</b> High Court Division,</p><p><b>Advocate:</b> Mr. Md. Abdul Haque, Advocate.,</p><p><b>Citation:</b>  2019(1) LNJ</p><p><b>Case Year:</b>  2018</p><p><b>Appellant:</b>  Md. Jahedul Islam Bhuiyan @ Jahed Mia </p><p><b>Respondent:</b>  Md. Abdul Rahim and others  </p><p><b>Subject:</b>  Code of Civil Procedure </p><p><b>Delivery Date:</b>  2019-11-27</p><!DOCTYPE html><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">HIGH COURT DIVISION</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center; line-height: 150%;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">(CIVIL REVISIONAL JURISDICTION)</span></strong></p><table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="MsoNormalTable" style="margin-left: 5.4pt; border-collapse: collapse; mso-yfti-tbllook: 480; mso-padding-alt: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;"><tbody><tr style="mso-yfti-irow: 0; mso-yfti-firstrow: yes; mso-yfti-lastrow: yes;"><td style="width: 106.0pt; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top" width="141"><p class="MsoHeading8" style="margin: 0in -1.4pt 6.0pt 0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.3pt; font-style: normal; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Md. Rezaul Hasan, J</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"> </strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-right: -1.45pt; text-align: center;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Judgment on</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">09.12.2018</span></strong></p></td><td style="width: 15.6pt; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" width="21"><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 150%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%; mso-ansi-language: EN-US; mso-fareast-language: EN-US;">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-ansi-language: EN-US; mso-fareast-language: EN-US;">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-ansi-language: EN-US; mso-fareast-language: EN-US;">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><a href="file:///H:/article/Issue__March__19(1)/Issue%20__March__19__C.%20R.%207%20of%2017_Md.%20Rezaul%20Hasan,%20J__5.doc#_ftn1" name="_ftnref1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><span class="MsoFootnoteReference"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: Symbol; mso-ascii-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-hansi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN-US; mso-fareast-language: EN-US; mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;"><span style="mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;">}</span></span></span></a></p></td><td style="width: 94.05pt; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" width="125"><p class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Md. Jahedul Islam Bhuiyan @ Jahed Mia</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: right;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 10.0pt;">. . Petitioner</span></em></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">-Versus-</span></strong></p><p class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: Mangal; mso-ansi-language: EN-US; mso-fareast-language: EN-US;">Md. Abdul Rahim and others </span></p><p align="right" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: right;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: Mangal; mso-ansi-language: EN-US; mso-fareast-language: EN-US;">. . . -Opposite party.</span></em></strong></p></td></tr></tbody></table><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 120%; tab-stops: right 210.25pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 120%; color: white; mso-color-alt: windowtext;">Code of Civil Procedure (V of 1908)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 120%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 120%;">Section 151</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 120%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 120%;">Order 47</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 120%; tab-stops: right 207.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 120%;">A review of a decree or order or a decision essentially contemplates prior and complete adjudication of an issue on merit. While an order obtained by exercising fraud or any order which is the result of any mistake of clerical nature, done on the part of the court, can always be corrected by the court, even under section 151 of the Code of Civil Procedure. In an application for review three preconditions are to be satisfied, namely- (1) discovery of new and important matter which was not within the knowledge or could not be produced by the aggrieved person inspite of exercise of due diligence, (II) any mistake or error apparent on the face of the record and (III) for any other sufficient reasons. The impugned order has been passed as if the succeeding judge was sitting in appeal over an order passed by his predecessor judge, while exercising the same jurisdiction. Thereby, the succeeding judge, in passing the impugned order, has usurped the function of an appellate court or of the revisional court, which does not vest in him. It is to be made clear that, the appellate court, in the course of deciding the appeal, shall consider the issues as regards the admissibility and weight of the evidence to be placed before it. The possession, however long it might be, if rooted in any unlawful acts or any kind of force or is an act of trespass, the same will not confer any right or title to the trespassers or to the unlawful occupier or the usurper, because the law will not perpetuate any illegality simply because of elapse of time.</span><span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">      </span>. . . </strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 120%;">(9, 10 and 12 to 14)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Government of Bangladesh, represented by the Secretary, Ministry of Industries and others Vs</span>.</em></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"> Shafi A. Chowdhury and others</span>,</em></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"> 47 DLR (HCD)</span> </em></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">567; Shah Mohammad Vs</span>. </em></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Ghulam and another 22 DLR</span> </em></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">(SC)</span> </em></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">102 ref.</span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; line-height: 120%; tab-stops: center 4.0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 120%;">Mr. Md. Abdul Haque, Advocate.</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; line-height: 120%; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .5in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 120%;">. . . For the petitioner.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 120%; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 120%;">Mr. Md. Asad Ullah with</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; line-height: 120%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 120%;">Mr. M. Masud Rana, Advocates.</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; line-height: 120%; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .5in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 120%;">...For the Opposite Parties.</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: center; line-height: 120%; tab-stops: 333.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 120%;">JUDGMENT</span></u></strong></p><p class="MsoListParagraph" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 120%; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 120%;">Md. Rezaul Hasan, J. </span></u></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 120%;">This Rule has been issued calling upon the opposite party Nos. 1-9 to show cause as to why the impugned judgment and order No. 35 dated 05.09.2016, passed by the learned Joint District Judge, 1<sup>st</sup> Court, Mymensingh, in Other Class Appeal No. 205 of 2013, should not be set-aside and/or pass such other order or orders passed as to this Court may seem fit and proper.</span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 120%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 120%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 120%;">Facts, relevant for disposal of the Rule, in short, are that, the opposite party Nos. 1-9, as plaintiffs, had filed Other Class Suit No. 18 of 2011, for cancellation of deed No. 5893 dated 18.05.1964 on the allegation made in the plaint (Annexure-A to the petition). The defendant Nos. 3 has filed written statement in the said suit (Annexure-B).</span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 120%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 120%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">3.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 120%;">The suit was decreed in favour of the plaintiff-petitioner. Against the said judgment and decree of the trial court, the defendant No. 1 Md. Abdul Khalek Bhuiyan preferred Other Class Appeal No. 205 of 2013 and in the said appeal, the respondent No. 11, who is petitioner in this revisional application, had filed an application (Annexure-C) under Order 39 Rule 7 of the Code of Civil Procedure, on 15.06.2015, for local inspection of the property described to the schedule of the application (i.e. a portion of the property covered by the impugned deed).</span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 120%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 120%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">4.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 120%;">After hearing the said application, the appellate court, by its order dated 18.06.2015, allowed the application for local inspection and directed to pay Commission Fees, being Tk. 3,000/=, for the purpose of inspection. The respondent Nos. 1-9 have filed an application, on 30.07.2015, for review of the order dated 18.06.2015, whereby the local inspection was allowed. The previous order dated 18.06.2015, it appears from the record, was passed by another judge then presiding over the court of Joint District Judge, 1<sup>st</sup> Court, Mymensingh, while the succeeding judge, after hearing the said application for review, by its order dated 05.09.2016, has set aside the previous order dated 18.06.2015 that was passed allowing the local inspection.</span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 120%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 120%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">5.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 120%;">Being aggrieved by and dissatisfied with the said impugned judgment and order dated 05.09.2016, the respondent No. 11 i.e. the petitioner has filed this revisional application under section 115(1) of the Code of Civil Procedure and obtained the present Rule.</span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 120%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 120%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">6.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 120%;">Learned Advocate Mr. Md. Abdul Haque, appeared for the petitioner and having placed the petition alongwith the materials on record, he mainly submits that, the order dated 16.06.2015, whereby the local inspection was allowed was passed by the then learned Joint District Judge, 1<sup>st</sup> Court, Mymensingh, who was competent to hear the application.
