However, before depositing the commission fees, the respondent Nos. 1-9 have filed an application on 15.06.2015, the learned succeeding Joint District Judge, 1<sup>st</sup> Court, Mymensingh, who, by its order dated 05.09.2016, has set aside the previous order dated 18.05.2016 and, therefore, has committed an error of law, resulting in error in the decision and occasioning failure of justice, in that the previous order was passed by the same court and the said court has become functious-officio<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>and had no jurisdiction to seat over as a court of appeal on the previous order dated 18.06.2015. Besides, he also submits that, this was not a reviewable order and that if the respondents were at all aggrieved by that order dated 16.02.2015, then their remedy was to file a revisional application, but for non-filing of the same, the said order for holding local inspection dated 18.06.2016 has become final and conclusive and, as such, the Rule has merit and the same may be made absolute, he concludes.</span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 120%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 120%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">7.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 120%;">On the other hand, learned Senior Advocate Mr. Md. Asad Ullah, appeared alongwith Mr. M. Masud Rana, on behalf of the opposite party Nos. 1-9, submits that, this is a case for cancellation of deed No. 5893 dated 18.05.1964. Therefore, in this case, the application for local inspection was totally uncalled for inasmuch as the points raised for local inspection were not in issue before the court of appeal and, by the impugned order dated 15.09.2016, the appellate court has rightly set aside its own order for the reason that the application for local inspection was filed for proving the possession of the respondent No. 11 in the suit property mentioned in the schedule to the application for local inspection. He also submits that, the fact about possession could be proved by oral evidence and that this respondent No. 11 did not file any cross appeal against the judgment and decree of the trial court. Therefore, in passing the impugned order dated 05.09.2016, the learned Advocate proceeds on, the appellate court has committed no error of law, nor the impugned order has resulted in any error, nor the same is prejudicial to this added respondent-petitioner. In support of this contention, the learned Advocate has cited 2 decisions, one in the case between Government of Bangladesh, represented by the Secretary, Ministry of Industries and others -Vs- Shafi A. Chowdhury and others, reported in 47 DLR (HCD)567 and another is between Shah Mohammad -Vs- Ghulam and another, reported in 22 DLR(SC)102. However, the learned Advocate for the opposite party Nos. 1-9 has stated that this petitioner (Added respondent No. 11) has claimed title in the suit property on the basis of oral exchange and was interested to prove unlawful possession and therefore, the impugned order may not be interfered with. He also submits that this Rule has no merit and prays for discharging the Rule.</span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 120%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 120%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">8.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 120%;">I have heard the learned Advocates for both the parties, perused the application for revision as well as the judgment and order of <span style="letter-spacing: -.3pt;">the Court below and other materials in the record.</span></span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 120%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 120%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">9.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 120%;">I have gone through the provisions regarding review of the judgment and order i.e. Order 47 of the Code of Civil Procedure, 1908. A mere perusal of Order 47, shows that a review of a decree or order or a decision essentially contemplates prior and complete adjudication of an issue on merit. While an order obtained by exercising fraud or any order which is the result of any mistake of clerical nature, done on the part of the court, can always be corrected by the court, even under section 151 of the Code of Civil Procedure.</span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">10.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">On the other hand, in an application for review three preconditions are to be satisfied, namely- (1) discovery of new and important matter which was not within the knowledge or could not be produced by the aggrieved person inspite of exercise of due diligence, (II) any mistake or error apparent on the face of the record and (III) for any other sufficient reasons. </span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">11.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">On perusal of the impugned order dated 05.09.2016 it appears that, nothing of these preconditions were considered by the same appellate court, at the time of passing this subsequent order dated 05.09.2016, passed by a different and succeeding judge.</span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 120%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 120%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">12.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 120%;">I also find that the impugned order has been passed as if the succeeding judge was sitting in appeal over an order passed by his predecessor judge, while exercising the same jurisdiction. Thereby, the succeeding judge, in passing the impugned order, has usurped the function of an appellate court or of the revisional court, which does not vest in him. Besides, in the facts of this case, the court has become functus-officio after passing the order dated 16.06.2015 and the succeeding judge was not (even the same judge cannot) re-open the matter already decided by it, which is indeed functions of a higher forum, sitting in appeal or revision.</span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 120%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 120%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">13.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 120%;">The issue, as to whether an oral and unregistered Ewaj exchange is lawful or not, is a question of law, already settled in other cases by the Apex Court of the country and I need not make any observation on this issue, during pendency of the appeal in the court below. Besides, it is to be made clear that, the appellate court, in the course of deciding the appeal, shall consider the issues as regards the admissibility and weight of the evidence to be placed before it.</span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 120%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 120%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">14.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 120%;">It is also to be made clear that, the possession, however long it might be, if rooted in any unlawful acts or any kind of force or is an act of trespass, the same will not confer any right or title to the trespassers or to the unlawful occupier or the usurper, because the law will not perpetuate any illegality simply because of elapse of time. </span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 120%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 120%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">15.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 120%;">However, anxiety of this Court is that, the impugned order dated 05.09.2016 passed by the succeeding judge of the same court even after it has become functus-officio cannot be taken lightly, because this may open a floodgate, in other cases, to change an order, passed by a judge once he is succeeded by another judge, and this will create a judicial anarchy and will upset the entire judicial process and practices, which cannot be allowed by this Court. </span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 120%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 120%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">16.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 120%;">The decisions quoted above, on behalf of the opposite party, is not applicable in deciding this Rule. Here the point for determination is whether the impugned order is sustainable or not in view of the provisions of section 115(1) of the Code of Civil Procedure.</span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 120%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 120%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">17.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 120%;">Accordingly, I find merit in this Rule and the same should be made absolute.</span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.35pt; line-height: 120%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 9.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 120%;">R D E R</span></u></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.35pt; line-height: 120%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 120%;">In the result, the Rule is made absolute.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.35pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">The impugned judgment and order No. 35 dated 05.09.2016, passed by the learned Joint District Judge, 1<sup>st</sup> Court, Mymensingh, in Other Class Appeal No. 205 of 2013 is hereby set aside. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.35pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">The order of stay granted and subsequently extended earlier by this Court is hereby vacated.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.35pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">The Court below is directed to dispose of the appeal within soonest possible time.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.35pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">No costs. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Let a copy of this judgment be sent to the concerned Court at once.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 120%; tab-stops: 30.3pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 120%;">Ed.</span></strong></p><div style="mso-element: footnote-list;"><!-- [if !supportFootnotes]--><br clear="all"/><hr align="left" size="1" width="33%"/><!--[endif]--><div id="ftn1" style="mso-element: footnote;"><p class="MsoNormal"><a href="file:///H:/article/Issue__March__19(1)/Issue%20__March__19__C.%20R.%207%20of%2017_Md.%20Rezaul%20Hasan,%20J__5.doc#_ftnref1" name="_ftn1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt;">Civil Revision No. </span></strong></a><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt;">7 of 2017</span></strong></p></div></div></div></div>
745	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">Md. Javed Alam Vs. A. F. Alfajuddin Ahmed, (Muhammad Imman Ali, J.) </h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p><b>Case No:</b> CIVIL  APPEAL  No. 118 OF  2014   </p><p><b>Judge:</b>  Muhammad Imman Ali, J, Hasan Foez Siddique, J,  Mirza Hussain Haider, J,  Zinat Ara, J, Abu Bakar Siddiquee, J, Md. Nuruzzaman, J.</p><p><b>Court:</b> Appellate Division ,</p><p><b>Advocate:</b> Mr. M.I. Faruqui, Senior Advocate with Nazneen Nahar, Advocate instructed by Mrs. Mahmuda Begum, Advocate-on-Record,</p><p><b>Citation:</b>  2019(1) LNJ</p><p><b>Case Year:</b>  2018</p><p><b>Appellant:</b>  Md. Javed Alam </p><p><b>Respondent:</b>  A. F. Alfajuddin Ahmed and others  </p><p><b>Subject:</b>  Abandoned Buildings (Supplementary Provisions) Ordinance </p><p><b>Delivery Date:</b>  2019-11-27</p><!DOCTYPE html><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">APPELLATE DIVISION</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: center;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(CIVIL)</span></strong></p><table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="MsoNormalTable" style="margin-left: 5.4pt; border-collapse: collapse; mso-yfti-tbllook: 480; mso-padding-alt: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;"><tbody><tr style="mso-yfti-irow: 0; mso-yfti-firstrow: yes; mso-yfti-lastrow: yes; height: 112.85pt;"><td style="width: 104.9pt; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt; height: 112.85pt;" valign="top" width="140"><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 3.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Muhammad Imman Ali, J,</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 3.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Hasan Foez Siddique, J, </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 3.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Mirza Hussain Haider, J, </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 3.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Zinat Ara, J,</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 3.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Abu Bakar Siddiquee, J,</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: .25in; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Md. Nuruzzaman, J.</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Judgment on</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">16.10.2018</span></strong></p></td><td style="width: 16.1pt; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt; height: 112.85pt;" width="21"><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: center; line-height: 200%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: center; line-height: 200%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: center;"><a href="file:///H:/article/Issue__March__19(1)/Issue__March_19__C.%20A.%20118%20of%2014__Muhammad%20Imman%20Ali,%20J___AD___5.doc#_ftn1" name="_ftnref1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><span class="MsoFootnoteReference"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: Symbol; mso-ascii-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-hansi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;"><span style="mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;">}</span></span></span></a></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: center;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p></td><td style="width: 93.55pt; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt; height: 112.85pt;" width="125"><p class="MsoNormal" style="mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Md. Javed Alam</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: right; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">. . . Appellant</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: center; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">-Versus-</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">A. F. Alfajuddin Ahmed and others </span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">. . .Respondents</span></strong></p></td></tr></tbody></table><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; color: white; mso-color-alt: windowtext;">Abandoned Buildings (Supplementary Provisions) Ordinance, </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">(LIV of 1985)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Section 7</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: right 210.85pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The Court of Settlement, being competent to decide the matter of the abandoned character of the property, after due consideration of all evidence and facts presented in the case decided that the property in question was not abandoned. The Government was the competent party to challenge that decision. Any occupier of the property as tenant under the Government, within the scheme authorising the Government to manage the said property, has no <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">locus standi</em> to challenge the decision of the Court of Settlement. If the Government succeeds in establishing that the property was lawfully included in the list of abandoned properties, then only the question of transferring the property to the occupier will become relevant.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">           </span>. . .(20)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Code of Civil Procedure (V of 1908)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Order VII, Rule 11</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Abandoned Buildings (Supplementary Provisions) Ordinance, (LIV of 1985)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Section 7</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.85pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">The inclusion of the property in the abandoned property list by gazette notification dated 23.9.1986 is negated and that decision that the property was not abandoned relates back to the date on which it was included in the gazette. In other words, the effect of the finding that it is not abandoned means that it was not abandoned on 23.9.1986. Hence, transfer of the property </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.2pt;">by way of sale dated 18.10.1990 to respondent</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;"> No.1 is nullified since the property was not abandoned and, therefore, the Government had no authority to transfer the property. </span></strong><span class="FontStyle11"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">The decision of the Government to release </span></strong></span><span class="FontStyle11"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; letter-spacing: -.2pt;">the property from the “Ka” list of abandoned</span></strong></span><span class="FontStyle11"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';"> properties by Gazette dated 02.12.2004 has put a final seal on the matter. The abandoned character of the property having been established all the way to this Division and the challenges of the Government as well as the present respondent having been unsuccessful, there can be no doubt about the legality of the gazette notification dated 02.12.2004 and hence we find that the trial Court rightly rejected the plaint of writ-respondent No.1 under Order VII, Rule 11 of the Code of Civil Procedure. The judgement and order of the High Court Division is not in accordance with law and accordingly the impugned judgement and order is set aside and the judgement and decree dated 24.03.2006 passed by the learned Joint District Judge, First Court, Mymensingh in Other Class Suit No.03 of 2004 is upheld.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">                              </span></span></strong></span><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">. . .(21)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.5in; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 1.0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">For the Appellant:</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"> <span style="mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Mr. M.I. Faruqui, Senior Advocate with Nazneen Nahar, Advocate instructed by Mrs. Mahmuda Begum, Advocate-on-Record</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.5in; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 1.0in;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">For the Respondent</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">:</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span><span style="mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Mr. Mahbub <span style="letter-spacing: -.3pt;">Ali, Senior Advocate instructed</span> by Chowdhury Md. Zahangir Advocate-on-Record</span></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: center;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">JUDGMENT</span></u></strong></p><p class="MsoBodyText2" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: normal;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-variant: small-caps;">Muhammad Imman Ali, J:-</span></u></strong> <span class="FontStyle11"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">This civil appeal, by leave, is directed against the judgement and order dated 15.03.2010 passed by a Division Bench of the High Court Division in First Appeal No.161 of 2006 allowing the appeal. </span></span></p><p class="Style2" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span class="FontStyle11"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong></span><!--[endif]--><span class="FontStyle11"><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">The facts of the case, in short, are that respondent No.1 as the plaintiff instituted Other Class Suit No.3 of 2004 in the First Court of Joint District Judge, Mymensingh impleading the appellant and others as the defendants for declaration of his title to the land detailed in the second schedule to the plaint and for further declaration that the notice dated 24.12.2001 issued by Deputy Commissioner, Mymensingh (defendant No.1) in respect of the land detailed in the second schedule was void, illegal, collusive, without jurisdiction and not binding upon the plaintiff. The plaintiff stated, <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">inter alia,</em> that the suit land belonged to S.M. Rahmatullah and during Liberation War of 1971, he deserted the property and as such, the same was declared abandoned property under President’s Order 16 of 1972. The suit property was included in the ‘Ka’ list of the abandoned properties prepared on 23.09.1986. The present appellant filed an application under Ordinance No.54 of 1985 before the Court of Settlement for exclusion of the property from the abandoned properties list and the said application was registered as Case No.1019 of 1992 before the Court of Settlement and the case was heard by the<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>Court of Settlement, but the respondent-Government did not disclose the fact that the father of the applicant by practicing fraud made a claim that he got the property by way of auction purchase. Thereafter, the appellant on 10.12.1998 obtained an order from the Court of Settlement for excluding the <span style="mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">property </span>from the abandoned list. The appellant thereafter moved the High Court Division by filing writ petition for a direction upon the respondent-Government to restore the vacant possession of the suit property in his favour and obtained Rule <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">Nisi</em> in Writ Petition No.5021 of 1999. The High Court Division by judgement and order dated 04.03.2001 made the Rule <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">Nisi </em>absolute and directed the respondent-Government to hand over the vacant possession of the suit property to the appellant. Pursuant to the said judgement and order, the Government on 24.12.2001 directed the plaintiff respondent to hand over possession of the suit property within 7 days from the date of receipt of <span style="mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">the said notice. </span>Subsequently, <span style="mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">the </span>plaintiff-respondent herein was evicted <span style="mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">from </span>the suit property. </span></span></p><p class="Style2" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 109%; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span class="FontStyle11"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 109%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">3.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong></span><!--[endif]--><span class="FontStyle11"><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 109%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">The plaintiff-respondent stated that the Government took decision to <span style="mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">dispose of </span>abandoned properties and accordingly, the plaintiff applied for purchasing the suit property, and the appellant did not take any step to resist the sale of the suit property and the Government transferred the suit property to the plaintiff by a registered deed of sale dated 08.11.1990 for a consideration of Tk.1,01,091.00. Thereafter, the plaintiff took loan from respondent No.5, National Bank Limited and constructed a semi pucca structure on the suit land by spending about taka 20 Lac. The respondent-plaintiff on going through abandoned property list and records of the Court of Settlement discovered that by judgement and order dated 10.12.1998 it released the suit property from the abandoned properties list. In Writ Petition No.5021 of 1999, the High Court Division passed a direction upon the respondent-Government to hand over vacant possession of the suit property in favour of the appellant. The <span style="mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Deputy Commissioner, </span>Mymensingh thereafter, on 24.12.2001 issued a notice upon the <span style="mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">plaintiff directing him to hand over vacant possession </span>and on receipt of the notice of eviction the plaintiff preferred Civil Petition for Leave to <span style="mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Appeal </span>No.<span style="mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">226 </span>of <span style="mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">2002 </span>before this Division against the <span style="mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">judgement and </span>order dated 04.03.2001 passed in Writ Petition No.5021 of 1999. The Government also preferred Civil Petition for leave to Appeal No.2186 of 2001 before this Division against the said judgement and order dated 04.03.2001. In addition the plaintiff-respondent filed Writ Petition No.3817 of 2002 challenging the decision of the Court of Settlement in Case No.1019 of 1992 which had declared the suit property as not abandoned. The Rule issued in the said writ petition was discharged on contest on 14.06.2003, against which the plaintiff filed Civil Petition for Leave to Appeal No.963 of 2003 before this Division. By its judgement and order dated 27.08.2003 this Division dismissed both the petitions. The Government, was made party in the case before the Court of Settlement as well as in the writ petition filed by the petitioner and the Government had taken all necessary steps in support of the plaintiff’s case, but the Court found that the property was not abandoned property and accordingly, released the same in favour of the appellant.</span></span></p><p class="Style2" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: normal; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span class="FontStyle11"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">4.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong></span><!--[endif]--><span class="FontStyle11"><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">The appellant herein, as defendant in the suit claimed that after disposal of the plaintiff’s leave petitions by this Division, the plaintiff-respondent lost all sorts of claim over the suit property and the present suit was barred by the aforesaid judgement and, as such, the plaint was liable to be rejected.</span></span></p><p class="Style2" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: normal; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span class="FontStyle11"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">5.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong></span><!--[endif]--><span class="FontStyle11"><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">The plaintiff-respondent filed written objection against the application for rejection of the plaint, stating that, the suit property was released illegally by the <span style="mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Court </span>of Settlement in favour of appellant <span style="mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">as </span>he obtained the said order on the basis of some false and forged documents and that the Appellate Division did not dispose of the leave petitions on merit. The plaintiff further <span style="mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">stated that </span>the points which have been raised in the present suit were not decided in the writ petitions filed by the appellant and the respondents.</span></span></p><p class="Style2" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: normal; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span class="FontStyle11"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">6.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong></span><!--[endif]--><span class="FontStyle11"><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">The trial Court by its judgement and decree dated 23.4.2006 allowed the <span style="mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">application </span>and rejected the <span style="mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">plaint of Other Class Suit No. 3 of 2004.</span></span></span></p><p class="Style2" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: normal; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span class="FontStyle11"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">7.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong></span><!--[endif]--><span class="FontStyle11"><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Being aggrieved, the plaintiff preferred</span></span><span class="FontStyle11"><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';"> First Appeal No. 161 of 2006 before the High Court Division and upon hearing the parties the <span style="mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">High </span>Court Division by its judgement and order dated 15.03.2010 allowed the appeal.</span></span></p><p class="Style2" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: normal; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">8.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span class="FontStyle11"><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">Feeling aggrieved by and dissatisfied with the judgement and order passed by the High Court Division,</span></span><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"> the </span><span class="FontStyle11"><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">appellant</span></span><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"> as petitioner filed civil petition for leave to appeal No.09 of 2011.</span></p><p class="Style2" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">9.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Leave was granted on the following submissions of the learned Advocate appearing for the petitioner: </span></p><p class="Style5" style="line-height: 107%; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 5.5pt 0in 12.0pt 27.35pt;"><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">“That the transferee (Plaintiff) from the Government had purchased the suit property during the pendency of the claim by the petitioner before the Court of Settlement and the</span><span class="FontStyle11"><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';"> judgement and order passed by the Court of Settlement having been upheld up to the Appellate Division, the transferee would rise and fall with the Government and as such, he has no cause of action to bring the suit. She further submits that the Government has no right to transfer the suit property as the Court of Settlement had determined the character of the suit <span style="letter-spacing: -.2pt;">property to be not an abandoned property.</span></span></span></p><p class="Style1" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 2.4pt 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span class="FontStyle11"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">10.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong></span><!--[endif]--><span class="FontStyle11"><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">Mr.</span></span><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"> M.I. Faruqui</span><span class="FontStyle11"><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">, learned Senior Advocate appearing on behalf of the appellant made submissions in line with the grounds upon which leave was granted. He further submitted that the plaintiff is seeking a declaration of title of property which has already been adjudicated up to this Division and hence the trial Court rightly rejected the plaint. He submitted that the High Court Division fell into error in finding that there were issues which would be raised in the present suit that had not been decided by the Court of Settlement or by the High Court Division in the writ petition. He submitted that the only issue in the suit is the plaintiff’s title which he got by way of purchase of the property from the Government. But this issue is already decided inasmuch as the Government had no title in the property because it had been decided up to this Division that the property was not abandoned and, hence, the Government had no title to sell.</span></span></p><p class="Style1" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: normal; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 2.4pt 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span class="FontStyle12"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">11.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong></span><!--[endif]--><span class="FontStyle11"><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">Mr. Mahbub Ali, learned Senior Advocate appearing for the respondent submitted that </span></span><span class="FontStyle12"><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">that neither the Court of Settlement nor the High Court Division sitting in its writ jurisdiction can decide/ adjudicate the disputed question of facts as have been raised by the plaintiff therefore, the Civil Court is the only forum to redress grievances of the plaintiff as such, the appeal is liable to be dismissed. He further submitted that since, the case before the Court of Settlement was not filed within the stipulated period of limitation nor the original judgement of the Court of Settlement was found in the record therefore, judicial </span></span><span class="FontStyle11"><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">record </span></span><span class="FontStyle12"><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">was </span></span><span class="FontStyle11"><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">tampered </span></span><span class="FontStyle12"><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">with and fraud was practiced upon the Court of Settlement in having the property excluded from ‘Ka’ list and as such, without holding inquiry and trial and without thrashing out the allegations in the plaint it cannot be rejected. He further submitted that neither the High Court Division nor the Appellate Division decided the issues raised in the plaint on merit and the jurisdiction of the Civil Court is still open to thrash out the allegations. He submitted that the principles of res-judicata in writ matters, where decisions are made in a summary proceedings mostly on affidavits, it should not be applied with the same strictness as in disputes in suits or </span></span><span class="FontStyle11"><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">proceedings determined </span></span><span class="FontStyle12"><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">in Civil Courts. He submitted that since, the defendant-appellant obtained the judgement from the Court of Settlement suppressing the fact of the title </span></span><span class="FontStyle11"><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">and possession of the </span></span><span class="FontStyle12"><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">plaintiff in the suit property and wilfully and deliberately did not make the plaintiff a party in the proceedings nor the Government disclosed the fact of selling the property to the plaintiff by registered deed dated 08.11.1990 and delivered possession to him therefore, in any way the judgement of the Court of Settlement was not binding upon the respondents. He submitted that </span></span><span class="FontStyle15"><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">Government </span></span><span class="FontStyle14"><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">action in </span></span><span class="FontStyle13"><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">contesting </span></span><span class="FontStyle12"><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">the writ petition as well as filing of Civil Petition for Leave to Appeal No.2186 of 2001 feeling aggrieved only to the extent of imposing penalty at the rate of 20% interest on the rent in no way can be said to have been decided the matter finally rather, the conduct of the Government as well as the appellant in contesting the proceedings is clearly collusive one which are liable to be adjudicated in the Civil Court.</span></span></p><p class="Style1" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: normal; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 2.4pt 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span class="FontStyle11"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">12.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong></span><!--[endif]--><span class="FontStyle11"><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">We have considered the submissions of the learned Advocates for the parties concerned, perused the impugned judgement and order of the High Court Division and other connected papers on record.</span></span></p><p class="Style1" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt 33.6pt; margin: 0in 2.1pt 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Bookman Old Style'; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Bookman Old Style';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">13.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">    </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span class="FontStyle11"><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">The property in question was listed as an abandoned property in the Gazette (Extra Ordinary) dated 23.9.1986 at page 9762 (70) Sl. No.9 in the ‘Ka’ list. Javed Alam son of the original owner, namely S.M. Rahmatullah (deceased) filed a case before the First Court of Settlement on 08.01.1987 for releasing the </span></span><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif; font-size: 11pt;">property from the list of abandoned properties. The case was subsequently transferred to the Second Court of Settlement and numbered as Settlement Case No.1019 of 1992. In due course after hearing, the abandoned property case was decided in favour of Md. Javed Alam by order dated 10.12.1998. Due to the inaction of the concerned authority in releasing the property and handing over possession to him, Md. Javed Alam filed Writ Petition No.5021 of 1999. The Rule </span><em style="font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif; font-size: 11pt;">Nisi</em><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif; font-size: 11pt;"> obtained by the writ petitioner was made absolute by judgement and order dated 04.03.2001 by which the Government of Bangladesh-respondent No.3 was directed to comply with the judgement and order dated 10.12.1998 passed in Settlement Case No. 1019 of 1992 by evicting the unauthorised occupants and also to pay rent to the owner of the property with a direction to pay interest at 20% of the rent actually received by the Government in respect of the property in question from the date of unauthorised occupation till the date of restoration of possession thereof.</span></p><p class="Style1" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: normal; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt 33.6pt; margin: 0in 2.1pt 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span class="FontStyle11"><strong><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif;">14.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong></span><!--[endif]--><span class="FontStyle11"><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">The Government respondent, by filing Civil Petition for Leave to Appeal No.2186 of 2001, did not challenge the legality of the decision of the Court of Settlement which had found that the property was not abandoned, but challenged the direction of the High Court Division to pay interest at 20% on the rent actually received by the Government from the date of unauthorised occupation till the date of restoration of possession. This Division disposed of the said civil petition maintaining the judgement of the High Court Division except the part wherein direction had been given to the Government to pay interest @20% per annum on the rent actually received from the date of unauthorised occupation till the date of restoration of possession, which was deleted. However, it was made clear that “the rent actually received by the Government from the date of unauthorized occupation till the date of restoration of possession should be paid to the respondent. The other part of the judgement i.e. making direction to restore vacant possession of the property in question to the respondent is maintained.”</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 0in 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span class="FontStyle11"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Book Antiqua';">15.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong></span><!--[endif]--><span class="FontStyle11"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">Thereafter, the Government released the property in question from the “Ka” list of the abandoned properties list by Gazette dated 02.12.2004. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 0in 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span class="FontStyle11"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Book Antiqua';">16.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong></span><!--[endif]--><span class="FontStyle11"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">It appears from the records that the present respondent A.F. Alfajuddin Ahmed filed Writ Petition No. 3817 of 2002 challenging the decision of the Court of Settlement dated 10.12.1998 passed in Settlement Case No. 1019 of 1992 claiming that he having been put into possession of the property in question by the Government was given the option to purchase the property, which he did by registered deed of sale dated 18.11.1990 and that all of a sudden he received notice dated 24.11.2001 directing him to hand over vacant possession of the property to Md. Javed Alam. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 0in 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span class="FontStyle11"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Book Antiqua';">17.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong></span><!--[endif]--><span class="FontStyle11"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">In due course after hearing the parties the Rule was discharged by reference to the judgement and order of this Division in Civil Petition for Leave to Appeal No. 2186 of 2001 where it was held:</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 0in 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 27.0pt;"><span class="FontStyle11"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">“The other part of the judgement, i.e. in making direction to restore vacant possession of the property in question to the respondents is maintained.” The High Court Division also observed that it cannot interfere with the decision of the Court of Settlement passed in Settlement Case No. 1019 of 1992 since civil petition for leave to appeals filed by the writ-petitioner is pending before the Appellate Division. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 0in 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span class="FontStyle11"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Book Antiqua';">18.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong></span><!--[endif]--><span class="FontStyle11"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">We find from the records that Writ respondent A.F. Alfajuddin Ahmed had filed Civil Petition for Leave to Appeal No.226 of 2002 and No.963 of 2003 challenging the judgement and order dated 04.03.2001 and 14.06.2003 passed by the High Court Division in writ petition Nos. 5021 of 1999 and 3817 of 2002. By order dated 27.08.2003 both leave petitions were dismissed. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 0in 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span class="FontStyle11"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Book Antiqua';">19.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong></span><!--[endif]--><span class="FontStyle11"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">From the above facts and circumstances it transpires that the decision of the Court of Settlement in Settlement Case No. 1019 of 1992 was challenged both by the present respondent No.1, A.F. Alfajuddin Ahmed as well as by the Government and the challenges have been unsuccessful up to this Division and subsequently the property was released by the Government vide gazette notification dated 02.12.2004. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 0in 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span class="FontStyle11"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Book Antiqua';">20.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong></span><!--[endif]--><span class="FontStyle11"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">It must be borne in mind that the claim of the writ respondent No.1 depends entirely on the success of the claim put forward by the Government with respect to the abandoned character of the property in question. We find from the records that the Court of Settlement, being competent to decide the matter of the abandoned character of the property, after due consideration of all evidence and facts presented in the case decided that the property in question was not abandoned. The Government was the competent party to challenge that decision. Any occupier of the property as tenant under the Government, within the scheme authorising the Government to manage the said property, has no <em>locus standi</em> to challenge the decision of the Court of Settlement. If the Government succeeds in establishing that the property was lawfully included in the list of abandoned properties, then only the question of transferring the property to the occupier will become relevant. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 0in 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span class="FontStyle11"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Book Antiqua';">21.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong></span><!--[endif]--><span class="FontStyle11"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">The effect of the decision of the Court of Settlement that the property was not abandoned is that the inclusion of the property in the abandoned property list by gazette notification dated 23.9.1986 is negated and that decision that the property was not abandoned relates back to the date on which it was included in the gazette. In other words, the effect of the finding that it is not abandoned means that it was not abandoned on 23.9.1986. Hence, transfer of the property by way of sale dated 18.10.1990 to respondent No.1 is nullified since the property was not abandoned and, therefore, the Government had no authority to transfer the property. It is curious that the Government did not mention the sale of the property at any point in time during the proceedings before the Court of Settlement or indeed when the matter was pending before the High Court Division. When the Government came before this Division, only the direction of the High Court Division with regard to interest to be paid on the rental amount was challenged. In our view the decision of the Government to release the property from the “Ka” list of abandoned properties by Gazette dated 02.12.2004 has put a final seal on the matter. The abandoned character of the property having been established all the way to this Division and the challenges of the Government as well as the present respondent having been unsuccessful, there can be no doubt about the legality of the gazette notification dated 02.12.2004 and hence we find that the trial Court rightly rejected the plaint of writ-respondent No.1 under Order VII, Rule 11 of the Code of Civil Procedure. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 0in 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 8.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span class="FontStyle11"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Book Antiqua';">22.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong></span><!--[endif]--><span class="FontStyle11"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">In view of the above discussion, we find that the judgement and order of the High Court Division is not in accordance with law and accordingly the impugned judgement and order is set aside and the judgement and decree dated 24.03.2006 passed by the learned Joint District Judge, First Court, Mymensingh in Other Class Suit No.03 of 2004 is upheld. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 0in 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 8.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">23.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span class="FontStyle11"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">In the result the appeal is allowed, without however, any order as to costs.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 31.5pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Times-Roman;">           Ed. </span></strong></p><div style="mso-element: footnote-list;"><!-- [if !supportFootnotes]--><br clear="all"/><hr align="left" size="1" width="33%"/><!--[endif]--><div id="ftn1" style="mso-element: footnote;"><p class="MsoNormal"><a href="file:///H:/article/Issue__March__19(1)/Issue__March_19__C.%20A.%20118%20of%2014__Muhammad%20Imman%20Ali,%20J___AD___5.doc#_ftnref1" name="_ftn1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; color: black;">CIVIL<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>APPEAL<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>No. 118 OF<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>2014</span></u></strong></a><u> </u></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 9.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt; color: black; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">(From the judgement and order dated 15th of March, 2010 passed by the High Court Division in First Appeal No.161 of 2006)</span></p></div></div></div></div>
746	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">Md. Mobarak Hossain Vs. SBS Cables Ltd., (Muhammad Imman Ali, J.) </h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p><b>Case No:</b> CIVIL PETITION FOR LEAVE TO APPEAL Nos. 1572-1574 OF 2018   </p><p><b>Judge:</b>  Syed Mahmud Hossain, C.J.  Muhammad Imman Ali, J, Hasan Foez Siddique, J,  Mirza Hussain Haider, J </p><p><b>Court:</b> Appellate Division ,</p><p><b>Advocate:</b> Mr. Rokanuddin Mahmud, Senior Advocate, instructed by Mr. Bivas Chandra Biswas, Advocate-on-Record ,</p><p><b>Subject:</b>  Companies Act </p><p><b>Delivery Date:</b>  2019-11-27</p><!DOCTYPE html><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; font-family: Symbol; mso-ascii-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-hansi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;"><span style="mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;">}</span></span></span></a></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: center; line-height: 200%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: center; line-height: 200%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: center;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p></td><td style="width: 93.55pt; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt; height: 112.85pt;" width="125"><p class="MsoNormal" style="mso-pagination: none; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Md. Mobarak Hossain<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span></span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; mso-pagination: none; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">. . . <u>Petitioner</u></span></strong></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: right; mso-pagination: none; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 9.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt;">(In all the cases)</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: center; mso-pagination: none; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">-Versus-<u></u></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="mso-pagination: none; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">SBS Cables Limited and others </span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; mso-pagination: none; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">. . . <u>Respondents</u></span></strong></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: right; mso-pagination: none; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 9.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt;">(In CP No.1572 of 18)<u></u></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="mso-pagination: none; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Paradise Metallurgical Complex Limited and others</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; mso-pagination: none; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">. . . <u>Respondents</u></span></strong></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: right; mso-pagination: none; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 9.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt;">(In CP No.1573 of 18)<u></u></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; mso-pagination: none; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Paradise Cables Limited, Banani, Dhaka and others</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; mso-pagination: none; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">. . .<u>Respondents</u></span></strong></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 9.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt;">(In CP No.1574 of 18)</span></em></p></td></tr></tbody></table><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; color: white; mso-color-alt: windowtext; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Companies Act (XVIII of 1</span></strong><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">994)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Section 110(1)(2)(3)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: right 210.85pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">In the facts and circumstances as detailed in the materials on record the High Court Division rightly found that there was adequate substance in the allegations that the petitioner's interest runs contrary to the interest of the respondent group of companies; that he had been using his position as Managing Director of these companies, his network as well as the brand name and goodwill of the "Paradise Group" in sponsoring "Star Paradise", established in the name of his son and daughter; that he has lost trust of the majority shareholders; that he was writing letters to bankers of the companies to hamper the business of the respondent companies; that his activities and conduct had led the respondent companies to financial hardship, shortage of cash flow and that created a deadlock situation in the business of "Paradise Group", since the banks were discouraged and prevented from opening L.C. or to give other credit facilities to the companies of the Paradise Group; and that he was leading these companies to financial sickness. The High Court Division also found that his unfair conduct is proved by his letters dated 08.02.2017 and 27.10.2017, addressed to Standard Bank Limited wherein the petitioner has falsely represented himself as the Managing Director of the companies, though he was not, and in which he had requested the bank to cancel 3 (three) letters of credit. Besides, the allegations of creating two forged resolutions dated 20.04.2016 and 04.11.2016 sent to the banker of these companies tantamount to extreme breach of fiduciary duties by the petitioner. He even did not pay any heed to the request made to him by other directors in the Board meeting dated 17.04.2017 to sign necessary documents and papers for issuing PG, BG and L/C and other credit facilities all of which were indispensable to run the respondent companies as going concern. Hence, the allegation that the petitioner was unwilling or unfit to continue as Managing Director is well founded.</span></strong> <strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">It appears from the record that in the instant case, though the petitioner is a minority shareholder, he however, had the upper hand in controlling and conducting the affairs of the companies, </span></strong><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.4pt; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">for more than 5(five) years. Hence, he cannot</span></strong><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"> be said to have been oppressed since he was at </span></strong><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.4pt; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">the helm of affairs of the companies. Therefore,</span></strong><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"> his prayer to buy him out is not considered as just and proper one. <span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">    </span>. . . (15, 16 and 17)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Companies Act (XVIII of 1994)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Section 108(1)(f)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: right 210.85pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">The High Court Division<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>correctly held that the Board meetings which could not be called to order due to lack of quorum were 'meetings' in the eye of law and the petitioner's deliberate absence without leave must be treated as 'absence' in those meetings and will attract the mischief of section 108(1)(f) of the Act and his office would fall vacant by operation of law, for which no resolution need be taken, save to record the fact of vacation of the office of the absentee in the minutes and to submit a Form XII to the RJSC and, thereafter, that director will not be entitled to receive any notice of Board meeting or to attend the meeting of the Board. The High Court Division further held that although the impugned Board resolution dated 16.02.2017 has become infructuous because of the order of stay and the subsequent EGM decision dated 17.05.2017, however, the conduct of the petitioner in deliberately absenting himself from three consecutive Board meetings, so that quorum could not be formed and the meetings could not be called to order, amounts to absence without leave in the said Board meetings, within the meaning and for the purpose of section 108 (1)(f) of the Act and the impugned Board resolution dated 16.02.2017 was valid. Such conduct of the petitioner also amounts to breach of his statutory duties and it was clearly prejudicial to the interest of the </span></strong><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.4pt; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">company inasmuch as a director, by resorting</span></strong><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"> to any tactics or measures whatsoever, cannot lead the company to a situation in which it will become impracticable for the company </span></strong><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.4pt; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">to call or hold its Board meeting or any other</span></strong> <strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.4pt; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">meetings permitted or required by law.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">               </span>. . .(19)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.5in; line-height: 110%; mso-pagination: none; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 1.0in;"><!-- [if supportFields]><spanstyle='font-size:11.0pt;line-height:110%'><span style='mso-element:field-begin'></span><spanstyle='mso-spacerun:yes'> </span>EQ \F(<b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'>Forthe Appellant</b>,</span><span style='font-size:10.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:11.0pt;line-height:110%'>(In all the cases)</span><span style='font-size:11.0pt;line-height:110%'>) </span><![endif]--><!-- [if supportFields]><spanstyle='font-size:11.0pt;line-height:110%'><span style='mso-element:field-end'></span></span><![endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-pagination: none; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 1.0in;"><!-- [if supportFields]><spanstyle='font-size:11.0pt;line-height:110%'><span style='mso-element:field-begin'></span><spanstyle='mso-spacerun:yes'> </span>EQ \F(<b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'>ForRespondent No. 3</b>,</span><span style='font-size:10.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:11.0pt;line-height:110%'>(In CP.
